*** WEEKLY AUTOPILOT FOR THE WEIGHT LAB — 2026-07-13 —
RESTART: YES (dexter.py changed — this is the last restart this feature will
ever need), DEPLOY: YES (webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js — push_dashboard.py),
RE-PASTE: NO ***
CONTEXT: the Weight Lab (propose/approve confluence-tag weight changes) worked
but required a restart to arm every approval, had no way to approve several
proposals at once, and had no path at all for Kev's own judgment calls (only
the 3 vocabulary-verified tags could ever get a live Approve button — a manual
"I think ema13 is overweighted" instinct had nowhere to go). Three-part fix,
same propose/approve philosophy throughout: the explicit approve/confirm action
is retained on every single path — nothing anywhere can change a weight without
one.
PART 1 — HOT-RELOAD (no restart per approval):
  _CONFLUENCE_BASELINE = dict(CONFLUENCE_SCORES) snapshotted once, pristine,
  before any override ever applies. _reload_weight_overrides() replaces the
  old startup-only _apply_weight_overrides() — now called once per scan cycle
  (same spot as tunables.json's load_tunables()) and recomputes EVERY tag's
  effective value as baseline + summed file deltas FRESH every call. This is
  the detail that matters: recomputing from a pristine baseline instead of
  summing against whatever CONFLUENCE_SCORES currently holds is what makes
  repeated reloads idempotent (a +1 stays +1 forever, never drifts to +12 by
  lunchtime) and makes removing an entry a clean revert to baseline, not a
  value stuck wherever it last landed. Clamp stays baseline-relative
  ([0, 2*baseline+2]); missing file reverts everything to baseline (the normal
  steady state); malformed file changes nothing and warns once, not every
  cycle. applied_at is stamped on an entry's first live apply (migrating
  pre-existing entries that only have approved_at); the freeze window prefers
  applied_at, falling back to approved_at for entries written before this
  field existed. /api/weight_overrides' "active" flag now means "currently
  live-applied," not "present when the process started."
PART 2 — DIGEST + MANDATORY CONFIRMATION:
  A digest header appears once >=2 verified-significant proposals exist:
  count, a combined evidence table, one APPROVE ALL button, and "N proposals
  since <date>" (last_reviewed_at, stamped automatically by any approval and
  by a standalone mark-reviewed link for a week where nothing gets approved).
  Every apply path — single approve, batch approve, and Part 3's manual set —
  now runs through the SAME in-panel confirm step first (not a bare browser
  confirm()): CANCEL fires nothing; CONFIRM shows each tag's current -> new
  value and a visible "(clamped from X)" note when the clamp engaged, plus the
  freeze-reset warning, THEN fires the real write. Critically, those numbers
  come from a new server-side dry-run (/api/weight_preview) running the exact
  same clamp math the reload uses — never client-computed — so Kev is always
  confirming the true post-clamp value, not a guess that could disagree with
  the server. Batch approval (/api/weight_proposal/approve_batch) loops the
  identical per-tag validation the single-approve route uses
  (_validate_weight_approval), not a separate trust path — one tag failing
  doesn't block the rest, reported by tag.
PART 3 — MANUAL OVERRIDE EDITOR:
  A quiet, collapsed "Manual adjustment" section at the bottom of the panel —
  searchable dropdown of ALL CONFLUENCE_SCORES tags (not just the 3 verified
  ones the proposal pipeline is restricted to — manual mode edits Dexter's own
  CONFLUENCE_SCORES vocabulary directly, no labeller-vocabulary aliasing risk
  exists here, confirmed by Kev). Numeric input, clamp range shown, at most one
  neutral "FYI: current data proposes +1 here" line if a live significant
  proposal disagrees with the edit's direction — informational only, never
  blocking, and read ONLY from the already-cached /api/weight_proposal payload
  from page load, never a fresh regression run just to decorate this input
  (stale-but-labeled beats fresh-but-expensive; empty cache = no note at all).
  /api/weight_manual/tags is deliberately independent of the regression
  engine's cache/self-test gate — manual judgment must work even when the
  statistics engine is broken. Stored as delta-from-baseline (source:"manual",
  plus set_to:<value> for the audit trail); a second manual set for the same
  tag REPLACES the first, never appends; setting a tag back to its exact
  BASELINE (never its live effective value, which can be mid-clamp or stale)
  with no weight_lab entry present removes the manual entry cleanly.
  LEDGER HONESTY (the rule with teeth): a manual write for any tag that
  currently carries a weight_lab-source (statistics-driven) entry is refused
  outright — Kev specified this for the set-to-baseline case (otherwise
  deleting the manual attempt would silently erase that a proposal was ever
  approved); the same session extended it to non-baseline manual sets too,
  flagged explicitly rather than added quietly, because the identical failure
  mode exists there (silent overwrite, or a summed value matching neither
  record). Redirect message either way: undo the proposal in the pending list
  first. The two sources of truth are untangled only by an explicit separate
  action, never guessed at by the code.
VERIFIED: three standalone scratch-test files (no dexter import, project
convention) — hot-reload (12 checks, including 5 reloads of a +1 staying at
+1, never drifting to +5), Phase 2's shared validator + preview math (10
checks), Phase 3's manual-mode ledger rules (11 checks, both directions of the
rejection, replace-not-append, clamp both ends, cross-tag coexistence). All
33 pass. py_compile and node --check clean throughout.
END STATE: Dexter scans and trades; the shadow/labeller pipeline studies every
outcome; the regression engine proposes evidence-gated, vocabulary-verified,
capped changes that freeze after every approval until ~200 fresh records
accumulate; Sunday is one digest, one APPROVE ALL, one confirm against a
truthful server preview, live within a scan cycle; a Tuesday instinct is three
clicks through the manual editor, same clamp, same confirm, same hot-reload,
labeled "manual" forever in the ledger. Nothing anywhere applies a number
without Kev's hand and an honest preview of exactly what is about to happen.
STANDING DISCIPLINES (the two things only Kev can still break):
  1. Let the freeze windows fill. The machinery is now faster than the
     evidence — the ~200-record freeze exists specifically so approvals don't
     outrun what the data can actually support. Don't chase it.
  2. Keep Chev's system prompt under its ~5k-token ceiling (see the 2026-07-12
     entry above) and keep the DURABLE LESSONS bar high (recurring across
     different regimes, not just repeated). Both are structurally enforced
     everywhere else in the system except these two — everything else now
     defends itself.
NEXT (Kev, manual): restart Dexter — arms _reload_weight_overrides() and all
six new/changed routes, the last restart this feature will ever need. Hard-
refresh the webapp, open Engine -> Weight Lab, confirm the collapsed "Manual
adjustment" section renders. Sanity check: approve or manually set one real
tag, confirm the panel shows server-computed before/after, confirm it, then
watch for "[WEIGHT OVERRIDES] ... adjusted this cycle" in the Dexter console
on the next scan (~5 min) — no restart needed for that or ever again.
RESTART: YES. DEPLOY: YES (weight-lab.js). RE-PASTE: NO.

IMPORTANT FINDING (flagged mid-phase, resolved with Kev before writing code):
  the phase's premise was that reasoning-validation logic already exists in
  labeller.py, operating on labels_closed.jsonl. It does not — grep for
  "valid" (case-insensitive) in labeller.py returns zero matches, and
  labels_closed.jsonl's schema is pure triple-barrier price-touch data
  (label=+1/-1/0, hit_2r, realized_R) with no reasoning text field at all.
  The only reasoning-validation signal anywhere in the codebase is
  `reasoning_quality` in `_do_postmortem` (dexter.py) — Chev grading his OWN
  trade's reasoning himself, stored on chev_journal.json entries. Presented
  to Kev as a choice: (1) build on this self-graded signal now, honestly
  labeled as such, or (2) design a genuinely independent price-action check
  from scratch (a much bigger, undefined-scope project — there's no existing
  hook, and building one is basically pointing the invalidation-candidates
  engine backwards at history). Kev chose (1), with two explicit conditions:
  rename everything user-facing from "Learning Gauge" to "Self-Check Rate" so
  it can't be mistaken for an independent check, and log option (2) as
  flagged future work, not built now, deserving its own design pass first.
  Both conditions were followed exactly (see the docstring on
  compute_validation_kpi() and every user-facing string above). This is also
  why `compute_validation_kpi()` lives in dexter.py, not labeller.py as the
  phase originally specified — the data source is chev_journal.json (dexter.py's
  domain, via `_load_journal()`), and labeller.py has no relationship to that
  file; adding a cross-import either direction would be architecturally
  backwards (dexter.py already imports labeller.py in production).
OUT OF SCOPE, FLAGGED FOR THE FUTURE (Kev's own framing, recorded verbatim):
  an independent, price-action-based reasoning-validation engine — joining
  Chev's stated invalidation/thesis at decision time (chev_decisions.jsonl's
  "detail" field) against what price actually did afterwards, bypassing
  Chev's own self-report entirely. Deserves its own design pass with Kev
  before it ever reaches a Claude Code phase.
WHY: The Clone provably follows his playbook (a prior audit already proved
that); whether the playbook is making him a BETTER trader was invisible.
Self-Check Rate is the first number that tracks that, even though it's a
softer signal than originally assumed (self-graded, not independently
verified) — the honest naming keeps it from being read as more authoritative
than it is.
HOW IT BENEFITS THE PROJECT: Kev now gets one line per asset class, in plain
English, on the existing Performance tab, showing whether Chev's own
self-assessment is trending up or down across playbook revisions — with an
explicit, unmissable label that this is self-grading, not an audit. Because
the underlying rate/delta math is entirely server-computed (same discipline
as the Weight Lab's server-side preview), the frontend can never show a
number the backend didn't actually compute. The version-stamping addition
also means every future playbook revision now carries a real, comparable
before/after in the data, instead of just a vague "sometime, on some
version."

=== PHASES A–E COMPLETE — LEARNING GAUGE + ELLIOT'S SUGGESTIONS ===

FOR MY PARTNER — plain English, no code required to read this.

WHAT THIS BUILD IS: the system already had real "learning" machinery running
in the background — a statistics engine proposing confluence-tag weight
changes (the Weight Lab), a weekly playbook rewrite per asset class, and an
Examiner that shadow-tracks trades nobody took. What was missing was a
reporting layer: nothing told Kev, in plain language, what any of that
machinery had actually found. This build is that reporting layer. It reads
existing files, never invents new statistics, and nothing in it can approve
a change or write a trade parameter by itself — every actionable item still
routes through the same manual approval buttons that already existed.

WHAT CHANGED, PHASE BY PHASE:
  PHASE A (fossil playbook retirement) — went looking for any code still
    reading the old, frozen, pre-split playbook file from before the system
    had separate crypto/forex/stock playbooks. Found none — every consumer
    already reads the correct per-asset file. Recon-only, no code changed;
    documented so nobody re-does this check later.
  PHASE B (Volume Profile explainer) — the Clone (the fast escalation model)
    was receiving `vp_start` tags without ever being told what POC/VAH/VAL
    mean. Wrote a small, ready-to-paste prompt addition. Kev confirmed which
    version of the prompt was actually live and pasted the two missing
    sentences by hand (prompt edits are never made by Claude Code directly —
    Kev always reviews and pastes prompt changes himself in Open WebUI).
  PHASE C (Self-Check Rate) — added a new "Self-Check Rate" card (Strategy ->
    Performance tab) showing, per asset class, how often Chev's own post-
    trade verdict on his stated reasoning was VALIDATED. Important honesty
    note: this is Chev grading his OWN reasoning, not an independent audit —
    it's named and worded that way on purpose, because no independent
    price-action check currently exists (that would be a separate, larger
    future build). Also added a "playbook_version" stamp to every new trade,
    so this rate can be compared version-over-version as new playbooks roll
    out, not just as one all-time blob.
  PHASE D (Elliot's Suggestions) — added a single consolidated digest card
    (Strategy -> Overview tab, top of the page) that runs automatically
    after every learning session and collects: real Weight Lab proposals
    waiting on a signature, lessons Chev has personally flagged as recurring
    in his own playbook notes, confluence tags that are statistically
    verified but trending negative, and threshold nudges from the decision
    log (both directions: "the gate may be filtering out profit" and "the
    gate barely fires at all" — the second one is true right now, ~16
    gate-rejections out of ~4,700+ decisions, which is worth Kev's attention
    once exploration mode is eventually turned off). Nothing on this card
    approves anything by itself — the Weight Lab items link to the Weight
    Lab's own existing approve button; the threshold items just point at the
    manual tuning panel.
  PHASE F (tightening pass) — three small follow-ups found on a second read
    of Phases C/D: verified the per-asset split's symbol-based asset
    inference against the project's own canonical version (proven equivalent
    by test, not assumed); added the missing "idle gate" nudge direction
    described in phase D's own spec but not yet built; added a "Generated X
    ago" staleness label to the Elliot's Suggestions card so it can never be
    silently read as more current than it is.

WHAT TO LOOK AT FIRST: open the dashboard, Strategy panel, Overview tab —
that is Elliot's Suggestions, the new top-level summary card. Then Strategy
-> Performance for the Self-Check Rate card. Both are read-only and safe to
just look at; neither one can change anything by clicking around in them.

WHAT THIS DOES NOT DO (on purpose, not an oversight): no suggestion on
Elliot's card auto-applies. No weight, tunable, or prompt is ever written by
this build without a human clicking the existing approve control that
already existed before this work started. A genuinely independent (not
self-graded) reasoning-validation engine and a richer visual "Tag Health"
monitoring tab (sparklines, streaks, shadow-vs-real divergence per tag) were
both discussed and deliberately deferred as separate future builds, not
implemented here.

RESTART: YES. DEPLOY: YES (frontend files). RE-PASTE: Kev's call on the Clone
prompt (see PHASE B above) — already handled by the time this shipped.

=== 2026-07-12 — REDESIGN PHASE 1 COMPLETE — FOUNDATION: DESIGN TOKENS, ONE
CARD STYLE, KILLED INLINE STYLES, EQUAL TOOLBAR BUTTONS — RESTART: NO,
DEPLOY: YES, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: first phase of a multi-phase visual redesign pass (separate from, and
downstream of, the earlier "Phase 1 CSS modularization" documented in
webapp/README.md — that split the monolith into css/js files; this phase
builds ON TOP of that structure). Frontend-only, no dexter.py/engines.py/Chev
Prompt touched, no JS file touched (verified via `git status` — every changed
file is a .css file plus index.html itself). Goal per spec: make the terminal
look like it obeys one small set of rules (radius/border/bg/spacing/icon
sizing) instead of a different one-off per feature, with zero new features
and zero behavior change.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. css/variables.css — added 8 new tokens to the existing :root block (did not
   remove/rename anything already there): --card-radius (aliases --r-md, the
   radius most cards already used), --card-border (aliases --border),
   --card-bg (aliases --s1), --pad-s/--pad-m/--pad-l (6/10/16px, matching the
   majority of existing card padding so adopting them is visually neutral
   almost everywhere), --btn-h (26px, the existing .iconBtn footprint), and
   --icon-s (15px, the existing toolbar icon size). WHY: gives every future
   card/button one obvious place to anchor instead of picking a value by eye.
2. One card style — converted every plain "card" container found across the
   audited surfaces (.arsenal-card, .radarCard, .hypCard, .convictionMeter,
   .engineBlock, .deepStatCard, .dirBlock, .stratScoreCard, .stratGradeCard,
   .stratFeedCard) to reference --card-bg/--card-border/--card-radius instead
   of hardcoded values or the raw --s1/--border/--r-md tokens directly. REAL
   VISIBLE CHANGES (the two genuine inconsistencies this task exists to fix):
   .arsenal-card was on its own hardcoded palette (#13152a/#252840/6px radius)
   — now matches every other card's look exactly. .stratFeedCard and
   .deepStatCard/.dirBlock were on --r-sm (8px) while every sibling card used
   --r-md (12px) — now 12px like the rest. Did NOT touch .ideaCard (its base
   --s0 background is a deliberate hover-contrast device, not an
   inconsistency) or layout dimensions (widths/grid columns untouched).
3. Killed ~100 inline style="..." attributes in index.html — every one was
   either (a) moved into a new or existing named CSS class/ID rule in its
   component's own file, or (b) left in place because a JS file genuinely
   writes to that element's .style at runtime (verified per-element by
   grepping js/ before touching anything — tradeOverlayBar, overlayAnalysisPanel,
   the ovLabel* checkboxes, rsiObjSection, rsiPanelWrap, brainStateBarFill,
   radarBadge, chevOpenBadge, hdrPerf/perfSection/perfDirBreakdown/
   deepStatsGrid/regimeBreakdown/perfSipRow, longBar/shortBar/regimeBarFill
   widths, hypHistorySection's display property specifically — its other
   static props were still moved to CSS), or (c) the onerror image-fallback
   pattern (left byte-for-byte untouched, exactly as instructed). New shared
   classes worth knowing about: .stratSectionSub (the small trailing note
   after 9 different section titles), .stratSubCaption (the 3 System Over
   Time sub-captions), .tbBtnGroup/.label.flush (topbar spacing), .mlAuto/
   .flexSpacer/.hidden (generic layout utilities, css/layout.css), .hasDropdown
   (the 3 Layers-pane tool rows with a TF dropdown arrow), .ltbDrop/.ltbArrow
   (was literally duplicated inline 3x each, now one rule), attribute-selector
   color rules for the 8 drawing-tool color swatches and the 3 EMA dropdown
   dots (`.swatch[data-color="..."]`/`.emaRow[data-slot="..."] .emaDot`,
   keyed to attributes those elements already carried) instead of a duplicate
   inline color. ONE PRE-EXISTING BEHAVIOR NOTE, not fixed (out of scope for a
   CSS-only phase): #janeOpenBadge's `display:none` turned out to be static,
   not JS-toggled like its sibling badges (radarBadge/chevOpenBadge) —
   jane.js only ever sets its textContent, never its style. Converted
   mechanically to a `.hidden` class (zero behavior change from today), but
   flagging it here since it looks like a wiring gap in a different (JS)
   layer, not something this phase's scope could fix.
   ONE OTHER MINOR VISIBLE DELTA: #chatContextLine had both an inline style
   (9px, #2a2e3a) AND an unused existing CSS rule (8px, var(--txt3)) fighting
   over it — the inline one always won. Removing the inline style (per this
   task's own instruction) lets the pre-existing CSS rule take over, which is
   a ~1px font-size and slightly lighter color change on that one timestamp
   label. Its margin-left:auto was confirmed redundant (#chatHeader already
   uses justify-content:space-between) — no layout change there.
4. Topbar row-1 icon buttons made pixel-identical (leftToggle/strategyBtn/
   cmdPaletteBtn/rightToggle) — REAL BUG FOUND AND FIXED: css/components/
   toasts.css had `#rightToggle img.accentIcon { width:31px; height:31px; }`,
   an ID-specific override that made the Call-Chev icon visibly bigger than
   its three siblings (26px button, 15px icon) — now reads var(--icon-s) like
   every other .iconBtn glyph. .iconBtn's own width/height moved onto
   var(--btn-h); a new combined rule `.iconBtn svg, .iconBtn img { width:
   var(--icon-s); height: var(--icon-s); }` replaces the old svg-only rule so
   <img> icons (strategyBtn/rightToggle) get the same treatment <svg> icons
   (leftToggle/cmdPaletteBtn) already had. strategyBtn's redundant inline
   15x15 style was deleted outright (the new base rule already produces the
   identical size).
5. Cache-bust: every changed CSS file's <link> in index.html bumped to
   ?v=20260716-2 (command-palette.css and animations.css untouched this
   phase, left without a version bump since their content didn't change).
BENEFIT: the terminal's cards, buttons, and one real icon-sizing bug now
share one small, named vocabulary instead of a different guess per feature —
and the next phase (or any future edit) has one obvious place to change a
radius/border/spacing/icon-size everywhere at once instead of hunting through
a dozen near-duplicate declarations.
VERIFICATION: `git status` confirms zero .py/.js files touched, only .css
files + index.html. `<div>` tag balance unchanged (372/372, open/close still
equal — no markup added or removed, only attributes). Brace-balance checked
on every edited CSS file (all matched, no syntax breakage). Diffed every
`id="..."` attribute touched in index.html — none were added, removed, or
renamed (only class/style attributes changed), confirmed via a targeted grep
over `git diff` rather than eyeballing it. Every new class name referenced in
index.html cross-checked against its defining CSS file. No `node --check` run
— zero JS files were touched this phase, so there was nothing to check.

refresh the page (cache-bust should force a fresh CSS fetch) and confirm (a)
the Arsenal cards, Radar cards, and Strategy Dashboard cards all now share the
same corner radius/border/background look; (b) the four topbar icon buttons
(sidebar/strategy/command palette/call-Chev) look pixel-identical in size;

=== 2026-07-17 — REDESIGN PHASE 2 COMPLETE — BUG FIXES: DEAD SEARCH BAR,
ARSENAL TOGGLE, UNDO, COPY/PASTE — RESTART: NO, DEPLOY: YES,
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: frontend-only bug-fix phase. No .py/.jsonl/prompt file touched (verified
via `git status`). Two of the four tasks' own "current state" premises turned out
to be wrong once the actual code was read (per this project's own anchor-based-
editing rule, findings are reported here rather than blindly following the brief) —
in both cases real bugs still existed, just not the ones originally assumed.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. TASK 1 — quick symbol search (js/ui/watchlist.js). CORRECTION TO THE BRIEF:
   #quickSearchInput was NOT dead — it already had a keydown handler (Enter jumps
   the chart, Escape clears+blurs), just no dropdown/autocomplete. Built on top of
   it instead of replacing it: as you type, a dropdown under the input lists
   matching symbols from `groups` (the SAME canonical watchlist data every other
   panel already reads — searches all three groups, not just whichever tab is
   selected in the sidebar), matched case-insensitively against symbol or label.
   ArrowUp/Down move a highlight, Enter picks the highlighted (or first) match,
   Escape closes+clears+blurs. A non-matching query shows "No matching symbol —
   press Enter to jump anyway" rather than going silent — and pressing Enter with
   no dropdown match still falls through to the ORIGINAL raw-typed-symbol jump
   (preserved exactly, not removed). New shared `_selectSymbol(symbol, type)`
   extracted from the watchlist row's own click handler — used by the row click,
   the dropdown pick, AND the raw-entry fallback, so there's exactly one place
   that knows how to switch symbols instead of two near-duplicate copies (the
   second copy's redundant explicit `_updateChatContext()` call was dropped —
   `loadChart()` already calls it internally, confirmed by reading chart-core.js).
   New markup: `#quickSearchDropdown` div inside `#quickSearchWrap` (index.html).
   New CSS (webapp/css/components/hypothesis-tracker.css, where the rest of the
   quick-search styling already lived): `#quickSearchDropdown`/`.qsItem`/
   `.qsEmpty`, built entirely from PHASE 1's card tokens (--card-bg/--card-border/
   --card-radius/--pad-s/--pad-m/--shadow-md) — zero new colors invented.
   NOT FIXED (found, out of scope): the Command Palette's own `buildSymbolActions()`
   (drawing.js) calls a function named `loadSymbol(s)` that is never defined
   anywhere in the codebase — every Symbol entry in Ctrl+K silently no-ops via
   optional chaining. Deliberately did NOT reuse that name for the new
   `_selectSymbol()` (which would have accidentally "fixed" this dead code path as
   a side effect of an unrelated task) — flagging it here instead for a future
   phase to decide on purpose.
2. TASK 2 — Arsenal toggle. CORRECTION TO THE BRIEF: the click handler lives in
   js/ui/chat.js (~line 934), not drawing.js/panel-toggle.js. `#chevArsenal` (the
   old topbar drawer) really was deliberately retired 2026-07-05 with its cards
   removed as dead UI — left alone, not touched or deleted, per the brief's own
   instruction not to unilaterally remove retired UI. The button today doesn't
   toggle that old drawer at all (its `classList.remove('open')` call was a
   vestigial no-op — that class was never added anywhere and had no matching CSS
   rule) — it always opens the right Intel panel to its modern "Layers" tab. THE
   BUG: clicking it a second time just re-clicked the already-active Layers tab,
   which visibly does nothing — reads as "won't close." FIX: real toggle — second
   click while already open on Layers now closes the whole panel; clicking while
   open on a DIFFERENT tab switches to Layers instead of closing (matches what
   "open Arsenal" should mean). A genuine `.active` visual state was added
   (`#arsenalToggleBtn.active`, webapp/css/components/chart.css — a brighter
   version of its own resting gold-dim look, same convention as
   `#magnetToggle.active`). State sync is centralized in ONE place —
   `_syncArsenalBtnState()` (webapp/js/ui/panel-toggle.js), called from inside
   `_toggleChevPanel()` (every open/close path: rightToggle, intelCloseBtn, this
   button, Escape) AND from the tab-click handler (the "switch tabs while already
   open" case `_toggleChevPanel` alone can't see) — so the button's state can
   never drift out of sync no matter which of the several ways the panel gets
   opened, closed, or switched. Escape now also closes it (webapp/js/charts/
   drawing.js's existing global Escape handler), scoped to only when Layers is
   the tab actually showing (checked via the button's own synced `.active` state)
   — deliberately NOT a blanket "Escape always closes the whole right panel,"
   which would have been a bigger behavior change than asked for every other tab.
3. TASK 3 — undo. CORRECTION TO THE BRIEF: undo/redo/copy/paste were NOT missing
   — `undoStack`/`pushUndo()`/`_copiedDrawing` already existed, Ctrl+Z/C/V/Delete
   were already wired up, and most creation paths (draw-a-shape, paste, pencil,
   click-delete-near-hover) already called `pushUndo()` correctly. Two real bugs
   and two real gaps were found by actually tracing the logic, all in
   webapp/js/charts/drawing.js:
   a. Ctrl+Z had no `INPUT`/`TEXTAREA` focus guard, unlike its Ctrl+C/V/Delete
      siblings which already had one — pressing Ctrl+Z while typing anywhere
      (chat box, template name field, etc.) also fired a drawing undo. Fixed by
      adding the same guard pattern already used elsewhere in this exact handler.
   b. REAL BUG, not just a gap: dragging/moving a shape called `pushUndo()` in
      `mouseup`, by which point `mousemove` had already mutated the shape in
      place — so Ctrl+Z after a move just "restored" the identical already-moved
      position (a silent no-op). Fixed by stashing a full snapshot at the START
      of the drag (`mousedown`, new `_dragPreState`) and only pushing it onto
      `undoStack` in `mouseup` if the shape actually changed (a plain click with
      no real movement no longer burns one of the 10 undo slots on nothing).
   c. Two delete paths had NO `pushUndo()` at all — the right-click context
      menu's Delete button and the Object Tree panel's own delete button. Both
      permanently deleted a shape with zero undo capability. Fixed: one-line
      `pushUndo()` added to each.
   d. The Command Palette's own "Undo" entry duplicated the keydown handler's
      logic slightly differently and was missing `markDirty()` — a palette-
      triggered undo didn't visibly repaint the canvas until something else
      happened to trigger a redraw. Extracted one shared `_undoLastAction()`,
      used by both the keydown handler and the palette entry.
   BONUS — Redo (Ctrl+Y / Ctrl+Shift+Z): implemented, since it dropped out
   naturally once undo was centralized into `_undoLastAction()`/`pushUndo()` —
   new `redoStack` (same MAX_UNDO=10 cap), cleared on any new action (standard
   convention — a fresh edit invalidates old redo history), symmetric
   `_redoLastAction()`. Also added as a Command Palette entry.
   NOT FIXED (found, explicitly out of scope for an undo-focused task): keyboard
   Delete/Backspace removes the LAST drawing (`drawings.pop()`) regardless of
   which shape is actually hovered — a pre-existing, separate bug about WHAT gets
   deleted, not about undo. Also not fixed: the context menu's property-edit
   controls (width/fill/opacity/font-size sliders, color swatch/align/label-
   position buttons) still call `ctxApply()` with no `pushUndo()` at all — sliders
   fire continuously on drag, so a correct fix needs a "snapshot once per edit
   session," not one push per input tick, which felt like its own small design
   problem rather than a one-line fix; flagging for a future phase rather than
   guessing under time pressure.
4. TASK 4 — copy/paste. Verified already fully implemented and correct: Ctrl+C
   copies whatever shape is currently hovered (there is no separate "selection"
   state in this codebase beyond hover — confirmed by grep), respects the same
   INPUT/TEXTAREA guard as Delete, Ctrl+V pastes a time-offset duplicate that
   becomes the new hovered/selected shape, calls `pushUndo()` correctly before
   pasting. No code changes made — nothing to fix.
BENEFIT: the quick-search bar now does what a "Go to…" box should without losing
the raw-symbol-jump escape hatch; the Arsenal button behaves like an actual
toggle from every entry point instead of only ever opening; a moved or deleted
drawing can now genuinely be undone instead of silently no-op'ing; redo exists
where it didn't before, at near-zero extra cost once undo was centralized.
VERIFICATION: `git status` confirms only .css/.js files + index.html changed, zero
.py files. `node --check` clean on all four changed JS files (drawing.js,
watchlist.js, panel-toggle.js, chat.js). `<div>` balance 373/373 (up from 372/372
— exactly the one new `#quickSearchDropdown` div). Diffed every `id="..."`
touched in index.html — the only unpaired one is `quickSearchDropdown` itself (a
brand-new id, not a rename/removal of an existing one); no existing ID was
touched. Manually traced the full `/`-focus → type → ArrowDown/Up → Enter →
`_selectSymbol` → `loadChart` chain against the actual code (not run live).
KEV VERIFICATION CHECKLIST (needs a live look, not yet done by Claude):
1. Press `/`, type a few letters of a watched symbol — a dropdown should appear
   under the search box; arrow keys move the highlight; Enter jumps the chart.
2. Type something that matches nothing (e.g. "ZZZZZ") — dropdown should say "No
   matching symbol — press Enter to jump anyway"; pressing Enter should still
   attempt the jump exactly like before this phase.
3. Click "Chev's Arsenal" — right panel should open on the Layers tab. Click it
   again — panel should close. Open it, manually switch to the Chat tab, click
   Arsenal again — should switch back to Layers, not close. Press Escape while
   on Layers — panel should close; press Escape on any other tab — panel should
   stay open (only Cmd Palette/active tool/context menu should react).
4. Draw a shape, move it, press Ctrl+Z — it should snap back to its pre-move
   position (not stay where you dropped it). Delete a shape via right-click →
   Delete, or via the Object Tree's ✕ button, then Ctrl+Z — it should reappear.
   Try Ctrl+Y (or Ctrl+Shift+Z) after an undo — the change should reapply.
5. Console clean; deploy via `push_dashboard.py`, re-check on phone.
RESTART: NO (frontend-only). DEPLOY: YES — push_dashboard.py, files changed:
webapp/index.html, webapp/js/charts/drawing.js, webapp/js/ui/watchlist.js,
webapp/js/ui/panel-toggle.js, webapp/js/ui/chat.js,
webapp/css/components/chart.css, webapp/css/components/hypothesis-tracker.css.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

CONTEXT: frontend-only. Replaced the mixed emoji-PNG/unicode-glyph/hand-drawn-SVG
icon soup in the main terminal's toolbars and panel headers with one vendored
Lucide icon set, and replaced native title="" tooltips on those same controls

overlay (16 "ⓘ" info icons, its own tab-pill emoji, "What is this?" titles) is a

call to Kev in case he wants a follow-up phase for that dashboard specifically.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. TASK 1 — vendored icons. Fetched the real upstream SVG source for all 27
   icons needed (menu, search, flame, message-circle, magnet, list, trash-2, x,
   chevron-down, refresh-cw, zap, radar, activity, check-circle-2, bar-chart-2,

   licensed" — lucide-static's own license header says ISC, a similarly
   permissive license; noting the correction rather than silently calling it
   MIT. Chose the inline-SVG-sprite option (webapp/index.html, right after
   <body>) over a js/ui/icons.js module — a sprite renders immediately with no
   JS dependency or load-order risk, and every icon is a named <symbol id="icon-
   NAME">, so <svg class="icon"><use href="#icon-NAME"/></svg> anywhere on the
   page just works. stroke="currentColor" throughout, so existing color

2. TASK 2 — replaced icons. Swept every emoji <img>/unicode-glyph/hand-drawn-SVG
   icon in the topbar (both rows), the chart's floating controls (object tree,
   RSI panel, chart tool popup, overlay toggles), the left sidebar (watchlist

   icons exactly as-is (no Lucide equivalent exists for either). Left the

   rewrites the "Run Dexter" button's entire innerHTML twice (once to show

3. TASK 3 — delayed plain-word tooltips. New webapp/js/ui/tooltip.js: one
   delegated mouseover/mouseout listener pair on `document` (works for every
   current data-tip element and any added later, no per-element wiring) shows

   mouseleave/mousedown/window-blur. New CSS (webapp/css/layout.css) built

BENEFIT: the main terminal now speaks one consistent icon language instead of
three (emoji PNG / raw unicode / mismatched hand-drawn SVG), and hovering any

engine.js, plus a full re-check of every other JS file touched earlier this

ever uses classList/style, never innerHTML — safe to swap their inner markup.

webapp/js/ui/tooltip.js (new), webapp/js/charts/engine.js, and the CSS files
that gained new rules (layout.css, panels.css, trading-logs.css, toasts.css,
chart.css, hypothesis-tracker.css) — files untouched this phase (variables.css,
topbar.css, arsenal.css, chart-popups.css, intel.css, strategy.css,
weight-lab.css) were left at their existing version stamps.

=== 2026-07-19 — REDESIGN PHASE 4 COMPLETE — LAYOUT: LEFT TOOL RAIL, SYMBOL
HEADER, UI DENSITY SETTING — RESTART: NO, DEPLOY: YES, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: frontend-only. Three structural upgrades to the main terminal layout:
moved the drawing tools out of the topbar into a new vertical rail alongside
the chart; added a symbol header strip (name/price/24h change/24h stats)
across the top of the chart; added a Compact/Comfortable/Large UI density
setting. Kev made one explicit architectural call mid-task (Task 1): rather
than faking the tool rail's reflow with JS while leaving the watchlist
sidebar as an absolute overlay, he chose to convert #leftPanel into a real
flex sibling of #body — his reasoning: "the tool bar goes with the drawer"
literally, and a future split-view phase should get a clean flex layout to
build on rather than more JS-pixel-pushing patchwork to fight with later.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. TASK 1 — left tool rail + sidebar architecture change.
   RECON (done before touching anything, per Kev's instruction): grepped
   every CSS/JS file for anything assuming #leftPanel was an absolute overlay.
   Found exactly two things: webapp/css/layout.css's own #leftPanel rule
   (position:absolute + z-index, floating on top of the chart, never actually
   reflowing anything) and webapp/js/ui/watchlist.js's leftToggle click
   handler (manually re-positioning #priceInfo/#status's `left` style by hand
   to fake a reflow that wasn't really happening). Nothing else in the
   codebase depended on the old overlay behavior.
   CHANGE: webapp/css/layout.css — #leftPanel converted from
   position:absolute (floating overlay, z-indexed above the chart) to
   position:relative + flex-shrink:0 (a genuine flex sibling inside #body's
   existing flex row). flex-shrink:0 is required so #chartColumn's flex:1
   doesn't squeeze this panel's width under pressure. z-index dropped (no
   longer stacking above anything). webapp/css/components/panels.css's
   `#leftPanel.open { width: 280px; }` needed no change — works identically
   for a flex sibling as it did for an overlay.
   New webapp/css/components/tool-rail.css: #toolRail, a 44px-wide vertical
   flex column inserted between #leftPanel and #chartColumn inside #body (a
   real flex sibling, not position:fixed) — reflows naturally with the
   sidebar, never covers the chart. Redefines --icon-s/--btn-h locally (CSS
   custom properties cascade to descendants) so its icons come out larger
   (18px+ per the brief) than the topbar's, without touching those tokens'
   global values elsewhere. webapp/index.html: moved the 9 drawTool buttons
   + magnetToggle + objectTreeToggle + clearDrawings into the new #toolRail,
   keeping every id/class/data-tool/data-tip attribute byte-identical — zero
   JS changes needed, confirmed webapp/js/charts/drawing.js's click handlers
   all select by id/class/dataset.tool, never DOM position. Active-tool gold
   highlight (`.pill.drawTool.active`, webapp/css/components/chart.css) and
   Phase 3's data-tip tooltips both keep working unmodified. .tb-row2 shrunk
   to Indicators + EMA/RSI/BB/VWAP + Arsenal — still a full row's worth of
   content on its own, so it was kept as its own row rather than merged into
   row 1 (the brief's "merge if nearly empty" case didn't apply here).
   webapp/js/ui/watchlist.js's leftToggle handler: removed the now-wrong
   priceInfo/statusEl manual left-offset hack (double-offset bug waiting to
   happen now that #chartWrap genuinely reflows on its own) and added the
   same fitContent()/syncRsiCanvasSize()/_syncRsiAxisWidth() resize-sync
   triad webapp/js/ui/panel-toggle.js already uses for the right Intel
   panel, on the same 220ms-after-transition timing (matches #leftPanel's
   own 0.2s CSS width transition) — same open/close animation feel as
   before, chart genuinely re-fits now instead of silently keeping stale
   proportions. Two now-orphaned `transition: left 0.18s ease;` declarations
   (webapp/css/components/toasts.css, #priceInfo/#status) were removed as a
   direct consequence of this exact change — not a general cleanup pass.
2. TASK 2 — symbol header strip. New #symbolHeader (webapp/index.html, first
   child of #chartColumn, above the position-strip banner) + new
   webapp/css/components/symbol-header.css: symbol name and live price
   large/bold, 24h change in % and absolute (green/red via existing
   --green/--red tokens), then small muted 24h high/low/volume stats.
   New webapp/js/ui/symbol-header.js, wired at the SAME existing call sites
   Phase 12's "call-site wrapping" convention establishes — no new fetches,
   no backend/Python touched:
     - window.updateSymbolHeader(candles, symbol), called right after both
       existing updatePriceLabel(candles) calls in
       webapp/js/charts/chart-core.js (loadChart() and pollLatestCandle()) —
       covers symbol switches, timeframe switches (timeframe-load.js's tf
       button handler already calls loadChart(), so it needed zero changes
       of its own), and every live poll tick.
     - window.updateSymbolHeaderStats(stats), called from the tail of
       webapp/js/ui/watchlist.js's applyWatchPrice() (the single existing
       choke point for every watchlist price tick), but only when the tick
       is for the symbol currently on the chart. Extended applyWatchPrice()
       with an optional 4th `stats` param and extended its two ticker fetch
       call sites to pass through fields they already fetch and previously
       discarded: Binance's ticker/24hr gives real highPrice/lowPrice/volume/
       priceChange for crypto; Finnhub's /quote gives real day h/l/d
       (change) for stocks but NO volume field at all.
   LIMITATION (stated explicitly, not papered over): forex has no 24h ticker
   anywhere in this codebase (see the pre-existing "session open" comment in
   refreshForexPrices), and Finnhub gives stocks no volume. Wherever a real
   stat is missing, symbol-header.js estimates it from the chart's own
   candles already in currentCandles (last 24h of real candle timestamps, or
   the whole loaded range if there isn't 24h of history) and marks that ONE
   stat with a small "~" flag plus a data-tip tooltip ("Estimated from chart
   (no 24h feed for this symbol)") — visible in the UI itself, not just
   documented here. Ticker stats arriving between chart polls (they refresh
   every 1-3s vs. the chart's 5-15s poll) trigger an immediate re-render
   rather than waiting for the next chart tick.
3. TASK 3 — UI density (Compact/Comfortable/Large). webapp/css/variables.css:
   three new `:root[data-density="..."]` blocks redefining --btn-h/--icon-s/
   --pad-s/--pad-m/--pad-l plus the root font-size (16px/18px/20px) that
   every rem-based rule below scales from. The bare :root block (today's
   values) is left untouched as the Compact set and as the safety-net
   fallback if the density script never runs. Converted the 4 named
   hardcoded-px areas to rem (relative to that root font-size, computed as
   today's-px/16 so Compact renders pixel-identical to before this phase):
   topbar text (#topbar .label, .pill, .freshStamp — webapp/css/components/
   topbar.css), tab labels (.groupTab in panels.css, .intelTab in
   panels.css), watchlist rows (.watchRow .sym/.px/.chg — webapp/css/
   components/trading-logs.css). The tool rail needed no separate
   conversion — Task 1's local --icon-s/--btn-h override on #toolRail
   already makes it participate in density automatically.
   Control: new #densityBtn (Lucide "settings" icon, fetched from
   lucide-static and added to the sprite as icon-settings, same vendoring as
   Phase 3) at the far right of topbar row 1, opening #densityPopover (new
   webapp/css/components/density.css + webapp/js/ui/density.js) — a 3-option
   dropdown positioned the same way the existing #emaDropdown popup is
   (position:fixed, left/top set from the button's own getBoundingClientRect
   in JS), not a new positioning pattern. Choosing an option sets
   data-density on <html> + saves it to localStorage, then re-runs the same
   fitContent()/syncRsiCanvasSize()/_syncRsiAxisWidth() resize-sync triad
   Task 1 uses (via requestAnimationFrame instead of a timed delay, since a
   density change has no CSS transition to wait out — it's instant).
   SUBSTITUTION FROM THE BRIEF (noted, not silent): the brief asked for the
   data-density attribute "on <body>" — it's actually set on <html>
   (documentElement) instead, via a small inline <script> in <head>, because
   <body> doesn't exist yet while <head> is still parsing and the whole
   point of this snippet is to apply the saved density BEFORE first paint
   (anti-flash-of-wrong-size). Every :root[data-density=...] CSS rule
   targets <html> for the same reason — this is the correct implementation
   of the brief's intent, not a shortcut. Default is "comfortable" per the
   brief (today's sizing becomes roughly Compact; Comfortable is noticeably
   larger).
BENEFIT: the drawing tools now live next to the chart they draw on instead of
competing for space in an already-crowded topbar row, and the sidebar/rail/
chart genuinely reflow together instead of one panel floating over the
others. The chart area now shows at a glance what's live-priced without
opening the watchlist tab. Kev can now pick a UI density that matches his
own eyes/screen instead of being stuck with one fixed (and, per the brief,
rather cramped) sizing.

the ones touched this phase — chart-core.js, watchlist.js, plus new

index.html tag balance after all three tasks: <div> 377/377, <button>

=== 2026-07-20 — REDESIGN PHASE 6 COMPLETE — POLISH: HOVER FEEDBACK, SHORTCUTS
PANEL, TRADE P&L ON CHART — RESTART: NO, DEPLOY: YES, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: frontend-only. The closing phase of this six-phase redesign arc (Phase 1
foundation tokens -> Phase 2 quick-search/undo-redo fixes -> Phase 3 one icon set +
delayed tooltips -> Phase 4 tool rail/symbol header/density -> Phase 5 recon-only,
never built, no code landed -> this phase). Three tasks: universal hover/press/
focus feedback everywhere interactive, a real keyboard-shortcuts panel, and a
click-to-reveal P&L card on a live trade's entry line.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. TASK 1 — hover/press/focus. Audited every CSS file in webapp/css (all ~2,330
   lines, every component file read in full, not grepped) before writing anything.
   Finding: hover was ALREADY present on nearly everything (most components
   already had their own `:hover` rule with their own color), but :active (press)
   and :focus-visible (keyboard) existed NOWHERE in the entire app except native
   text-input focus rings. Rather than hand-writing a bespoke press rule per
   component (the brief's own "not per-component one-offs" instruction), added
   ONE shared block to webapp/css/layout.css: a `:where(...)` selector listing
   every interactive class/id found during the audit gets `filter:brightness(0.88)`
   on `:active`, and a separate `:where(button, input, select, textarea, a,
   [tabindex]):focus-visible` gets a gold outline. `:where()` deliberately keeps
   this at ZERO specificity so it can never out-rank any existing color rule —
   .active's own selected-state background is untouched, only a transient darken
   layers on top of whatever's already showing. Used filter (not transform:scale)
   for the press effect specifically because several components already animate
   `transform` on :hover (.ideaCard's lift, .emaDot's pop) — filter and transform
   are different properties, so both can be true at once (hovering AND pressing)
   with no fight over which one wins, which a transform-based press would have
   risked colliding with.
   SCOPE NOTE, not silently narrowed: the focus-visible ring only applies to
   elements already in the native Tab order today (real <button>/<input> — every
   .pill/.iconBtn/.densityOpt/etc. is one, confirmed by reading index.html).
   Several other clickable-LOOKING rows (.watchRow, .intelTab, .groupTab,
   .arsenal-card, .radarCard, .ideaCard, .layerToolBtn, .stratTab, .cmdItem,
   .qsItem) are plain <div>s with no tabindex — hover/press still work on them
   (those don't need focusability), but they're not keyboard-reachable at all
   today, so a focus ring on them would never be visible. Making them genuinely
   keyboard-operable (tabindex + Enter/Space activation) is a bigger, separate
   change than "add a focus style" asked for — flagged here as a real follow-up,
   not silently skipped.
   TWO TRUE GAPS found and fixed (not invented busywork — these had zero hover
   feedback of any kind before this phase): #resetBalance (webapp/css/components/
   panels.css) and .ovBtn, the Entry/Analysis buttons on the trade overlay bar
   (webapp/css/components/toasts.css).
2. TASK 2 — keyboard shortcuts panel. New #shortcutsOverlay/#shortcutsPanel
   (webapp/index.html) + webapp/css/components/shortcuts-panel.css (reuses
   command-palette.css's existing .cmdKbd key-badge style rather than inventing a
   second one) + new webapp/js/ui/shortcuts-panel.js. Opened via a new topbar
   #shortcutsBtn (Lucide "keyboard" icon, fetched from lucide-static and added to
   the sprite the same way every icon since Phase 3 has been) or the `?` key —
   added inside drawing.js's EXISTING guarded keydown block (same
   `!ctrlKey/!metaKey/!altKey/not-an-input` guard `/` and `R` already use, per the
   brief's own instruction to reuse it) so it can never fire while typing. `/`
   alone still only focuses search — `e.key` reports '?' only when Shift is
   actually held on that key, so the two checks never collide on the same
   keypress despite sharing a physical key. Closes via its own X button, clicking
   outside, or Esc (added to drawing.js's one shared Escape block, alongside
   every other Esc-closeable overlay — same pattern as Phase 2's Arsenal-panel
   Escape addition).
   Every shortcut listed was checked against the REAL keydown handler in
   drawing.js before being written down, per the brief's explicit instruction —
   one real discrepancy was found and deliberately NOT copied into the panel: the
   Command Palette's own ACTIONS array labels Radar with kbd hint "5", but the
   actual keydown handler's tabKeys map only ever had '1'-'4' (trades/engine/
   layers/chat) — pressing 5 does nothing. Flagging this pre-existing Command
   Palette inaccuracy here for a future phase rather than fixing it (out of this
   phase's scope) or documenting a shortcut that doesn't work.
   ALSO PER THE BRIEF'S OWN INSTRUCTION ("while there, verify Del/Backspace..."):
   found and fixed a REAL bug in drawing.js — Delete/Backspace was `drawings.pop()`,
   unconditionally removing the LAST drawing in the array regardless of what was
   actually hovered or under the cursor. Fixed to use `hoverIndex`, the exact same
   hover-based "selection" model this codebase already uses for Ctrl+C (there is
   no separate click-to-select state anywhere in this app, confirmed by grep —
   hover IS the selection), so Delete now removes whatever you're actually
   pointing at, matching Ctrl+C/Ctrl+V's existing behavior instead of contradicting
   it. Also added the missing `markDirty()` call (the old code relied on an
   incidental mousemove to trigger the next repaint; Delete has no guaranteed
   mouse movement after it).
3. TASK 3 — P&L on live trade lines (click-to-show). RECON FIRST (per the brief):
   traced how entry/SL/TP lines actually reach the chart across drawing.js,
   engine.js, and trading-logs.js/chev-corner.js. Found TWO existing rendering
   paths, not one: real LightweightCharts price lines (candleSeries.
   createPriceLine, chev-corner.js's _refreshTradeOverlayLines()) for the actual
   Entry/SL/TP/SIP lines, and a SEPARATE canvas-drawn layer (drawing.js's
   redrawAll() + engine.js's _drawLivePosition(), the latter already wrapping
   redrawAll a second time) that draws colored entry/SL/TP zones, small price-axis
   badges, AND an already-existing, ALWAYS-ON floating P&L percentage badge (with
   leverage) at the CURRENT price line. This phase's card is genuinely additive
   to that existing badge, not a duplicate or a replacement — it lives at the
   ENTRY line (not the current-price line), is click-toggled (not always-on), and
   shows more detail (R-multiple, dollar P&L, both stop and target distance) than
   the tiny always-on badge has room for.
   Live P&L in dollars ALREADY reaches the frontend — `t.live_pnl` is fetched and
   rendered today in the trade feed row (trading-logs.js's `.logPnl` span) — reused
   directly, no new backend endpoint, no Python touched. FOUND AND FIXED A REAL
   STALENESS BUG along the way: the code that keeps `_activeTrade` in sync with
   the live feed (trading-logs.js, ~line 182) only ever checked sl/tp/entry/is_sip
   for changes — `live_pnl` was copied onto `_activeTrade` exactly once, at the
   moment a trade was first clicked, and then silently never touched again. Fixed
   by copying it every refresh cycle unconditionally (kept OUT of the existing
   change-check that triggers a full price-line redraw, since P&L ticks far more
   often than price levels do and doesn't need one).
   BUILD: new #tradePnlCard (webapp/index.html, inside #chartWrap) + webapp/css/
   components/trade-pnl-card.css (position:fixed, JS-positioned at the click
   point — same convention as #emaDropdown/#densityPopover, not a new
   positioning pattern) + new webapp/js/ui/trade-pnl-card.js. Clicking anywhere
   along the entry line's Y (a full-width hit zone, matching how a horizontal
   price line actually looks — not just its price-axis label) toggles the card;
   clicking again, the X button, Esc, or clicking anywhere else all close it.
   Shows: direction + symbol, entry price, P&L as BOTH an R-multiple (computed
   fresh from the live chart price against entry/stop — always in sync with the
   live tick regardless of backend refresh timing) AND real dollars (the
   now-un-stale `live_pnl`), plus stop/target distance in % from the live price.
   Refreshed via the exact same call-site-wrapping hooks Phase 4 established for
   the symbol header (`window.updateSymbolHeader`'s two call sites in
   chart-core.js's loadChart()/pollLatestCandle(), PLUS trading-logs.js's own
   live-trailing block where live_pnl actually updates) — no new polling loop.
   READ-ONLY BY DESIGN, per the brief's own explicit safety requirement: the card
   has no button, control, or click target that touches the live trade in any
   way — it only ever displays numbers.
BENEFIT — SIX-PHASE ARC SUMMARY: the main terminal went from a single cramped
toolbar row and a mix of emoji/PNG/hand-drawn icons to a cohesive, tokenized
design system: Phase 1 established the shared spacing/radius/color tokens every
later phase built on; Phase 2 fixed real quick-search/undo/redo/Arsenal-toggle
bugs found by actually tracing the code rather than assuming the brief's premise;
Phase 3 unified every icon to one vendored Lucide set and replaced slow native
tooltips with fast plain-word ones; Phase 4 gave the terminal a real application
layout — a docked tool rail, a symbol/price header, and a genuine UI density
setting — converting the watchlist sidebar from a fake floating overlay into an
honest flex layout along the way; Phase 5 was recon-and-plan only for multi-chart
split view (never built — no code from that phase exists anywhere in this
codebase, a decision Kev can revisit any time by re-pasting that phase); and this
phase closed the loop with the small, cheap-feeling details — every control now
visibly reacts to touch, every shortcut is discoverable in one place instead of
living only in Kev's memory, and a live trade's real numbers are one click away
instead of buried in a tiny always-on badge. Two real, pre-existing bugs (Delete
key deleting the wrong shape; live P&L silently freezing after the first look)
were found and fixed as a direct result of this phase's own recon, not invented
extra scope.
VERIFICATION: `node --check` clean on every JS file in the project (not just this
phase's five changed/new files — drawing.js, chart-core.js, trading-logs.js, plus
new shortcuts-panel.js and trade-pnl-card.js). `git status`/`git diff --stat`
confirm no .py file touched. index.html tag balance: <div> 405/405, <button>
71/71, <svg> 58/58, <symbol id=...> 29/29. Zero duplicate `id="..."` anywhere.
Confirmed in code (not yet confirmed live by Kev): the `?` handler sits inside
drawing.js's existing input-focused guard (same block as `/` and `R`), so it
cannot fire while typing in any input/textarea. Cache-bust bumped on every file
actually changed this phase: index.html itself, layout.css, panels.css,
toasts.css, shortcuts-panel.css (new), trade-pnl-card.css (new), drawing.js,
chart-core.js, trading-logs.js, shortcuts-panel.js (new), trade-pnl-card.js
(new) — every other CSS/JS file was left at its existing version stamp.
KEV VERIFICATION CHECKLIST (needs a live look, not yet done by Claude):
1. Hover over pills/icon buttons/tabs/watchlist rows/arsenal cards — each should
   still show its own existing hover color. Click and HOLD on any of them — you
   should see a brief, subtle darkening while the mouse is down, gone the instant
   you release. Tab through controls with the keyboard (no mouse) — a gold

2. Press `?` anywhere outside a text box (or click the new keyboard icon at the
   far right of the topbar's top row) — a panel listing every real shortcut,

   it to close. Confirm every shortcut listed actually does what it says.
3. Draw a shape, hover a DIFFERENT shape than the one you just drew, press
   Delete — the HOVERED shape should disappear, not the one you drew (this was
   backwards before this phase).
4. Click a live open trade in the Trades pane so its entry/SL/TP lines and the
   position strip appear on the chart. Click directly on the gold entry line
   (anywhere along its width) — a small card should appear showing direction,

   freeze at the moment you opened it.

=== 2026-07-13 — SHADOW COMBO INTELLIGENCE (Ale's commit "Shadow Analysis
Included", 0710c1d) — RESTART: YES, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: backend-only, committed and pushed directly by Ale (not built or
verified by Claude — this entry documents it after the fact, from reading the
real diff, since the commit itself didn't come with a handoff entry). First
real bridge between the two previously-separate tracking systems: the SKIPPED-
setup "shadow" tracking (counterfactual_report.py / labeller.py, quarantined
in the UI as "optimistic, unconfirmed") and REAL posted trades. Up to now
shadow outcomes only ever informed the Strategy dashboard's own Shadow
Outcomes section — nothing fed them back into live trade-taking or the
periodic learning session.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. counterfactual_report.py — new `get_qualifying_shadow_combos(min_n=5,
   min_total_r=0.0)`: filters the shadow (skipped-setup) tag-combo leaderboard
   down to combos with enough resolved history (n>=5) AND a net-positive
   shadow result. Read-only, no side effects. Two new module constants
   (SHADOW_COMBO_MIN_N, SHADOW_COMBO_MIN_TOTAL_R) so both callers below share
   one definition of "qualifying" instead of each hand-rolling their own bar.
2. dexter.py, live trade posting (~13489) — when a new trade is posted, its
   Dexter-computed features (labeller.normalize_reasons() tokens — the SAME
   touch-count/pattern vocabulary as sr_multi/sr_single, never Chev's own
   typed tags) are checked against every qualifying shadow combo. If this
   trade's features are a superset of a qualifying combo, the trade is
   stamped `shadow_combo_match` with that combo's name (picking the
   highest-total_R match if more than one qualifies). Wrapped in try/except —
   a failure here can't block the trade itself, it just leaves the tag blank.
3. dexter.py, `_do_postmortem` (~5249) — `shadow_combo_match` is now carried
   into the closed-trade journal entry, so it survives to be read back later.
4. dexter.py, `_run_learning_session` (~4611) — new "SHADOW COMBO
   INTELLIGENCE" block in the periodic playbook-rewrite prompt: for every
   qualifying shadow combo, states its shadow win rate and total R, THEN
   cross-references the journal for any REAL trades that carried that same
   `shadow_combo_match` stamp and states their real W/L record next to it.
   The prompt explicitly instructs: label every claim "tentative (shadow
   only)" until at least 3 real confirmed trades exist for that combo — this
   is a real, no client-side-hallucination bridge, not a promotion of shadow
   data to trusted status. New section name added to
   `_PLAYBOOK_SECTION_NAMES` so this can appear as its own named block in the
   generated playbook file. `_REFERENCE_BLOCK_CHAR_CAP` bumped 1200->1350 to
   fit it (small token-budget increase, not a structural change).
5. labeller.py — unrelated small bugfix bundled into the same commit: two of
   the ordered reason-text-to-tag-token mappings had a real ordering/matching
   bug. "GP" was being checked before the more specific "[WATCH ...]" prefixes,
   so a string like "[WATCH — approaching GP] GP zone..." could misfire as
   the unrelated gp_sr_combo token instead of watch_signal. Reordered so
   [WATCH...] prefixes are checked first. Also: Dexter sometimes emits an
   em-dash (—) in these strings rather than a plain hyphen (-); the regex only
   matched the hyphen form, silently missing the em-dash variant entirely.
   Both the hyphen and em-dash forms are now matched.
BENEFIT: the Shadow Outcomes system stops being a one-way, forever-unverified
guess — setups Chev skipped that would have won can now be watched for their
real-world equivalent showing up in an actual posted trade, with an honest,
labeled comparison of "what shadow-tracking predicted" vs "what really
happened" once enough real trades exist. The labeller.py fix corrects a
silent miscount that could have been quietly polluting the gp_sr_combo tag's
stats with unrelated [WATCH] setups.
VERIFICATION: not independently re-verified by Claude this session (no
py_compile/self-test re-run) — this entry is a post-hoc write-up of Ale's own
already-pushed, already-pulled commit, based on reading the actual diff line
by line, not a build Claude performed or tested. Every new code path is
wrapped in try/except (the shadow-combo-match check at trade-post time
explicitly cannot block or alter the trade itself if it fails). Kev should
treat this the same as any other backend change he didn't personally build —
worth a real restart + a look at the next few learning-session outputs to
confirm the new SHADOW COMBO INTELLIGENCE block reads sensibly before trusting it.
RESTART: YES (dexter.py + labeller.py changed — the running Dexter process is
still on the old code in memory until restarted). DEPLOY: NO (no webapp/
files touched). RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO (no persona/prompt text changed,
Python logic only).

=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT RECALIBRATION PHASE 1: CURRENT_WEIGHTS populated in weight_proposal.py — RESTART: NOT REQUIRED, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: weight_proposal.py (the confluence-tag marginal-effect proposal
report, added earlier this project) had an intentionally-empty
CURRENT_WEIGHTS = {} dict — it refused to propose a weight change for any tag
it didn't know the current point value of, by design (guardrail: never guess
what "current" means). This phase filled that dict in by hand, so the report
now actually produces proposals instead of "n/a" in the CUR_W column.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. Read labeller.py's REASON_MAP_ORDERED + normalize_reasons() to get the
   full list of feature tokens that can appear in labels_closed.jsonl's
   "features" list (sr_multi/sr_single, fib_*, ema*, bb_*, vp_*, rsi_*,
   sweep, pattern_*, oi_*, funding_extreme, fast_anchor_*, watch_signal,
   gp_sr_combo, gp, other).
2. Read dexter.py's scan_pair_tf() (~line 8826) and derivs.py's
   classify_derivs() (~line 70) — the actual functions that build the reason
   strings these tokens come from — to find each one's real current point
   value in the running code, not CONFLUENCE_SCORES (a different, TF-based
   vocabulary Chev's own typed tags use, e.g. sr_4h/sr_1h — confirmed a
   separate system earlier this project).
3. Mapped 29 tags into CURRENT_WEIGHTS with a sourced comment on every line
   (sr_multi=3, sr_single=2, gp=4, fib_618=2, fib_50=2, fib_786=1,
   fib_other=1, ema55=2.0, ema21=1.0, ema13=0.5, ema_cross=1, bb_near=0.5,
   bb_mid=1.0, bb_squeeze=0, rsi_ob=0.5, rsi_os=0.5, rsi_50_cross=0, sweep=3,
   pattern_breakout=2.0, pattern_breakout_vol=3.0, pattern_high_conf=1.5,
   oi_divergence=1.5, oi_confirm=1.0, the four fast_anchor_* tags=0,
   watch_signal=0).
4. Left 9 tags deliberately UNMAPPED (documented in a comment block above the
   dict) because their real dexter.py weight isn't a single fixed number:
   gp_sr_combo (×1.15 multiplier, not additive), bb_burst and vp_poc/vah/val
   (depend on which timeframe is primary, VP also on anchor-confirmation),
   the four rsi_div* tokens (all route through a dynamic _div_strength_score
   function), funding_extreme (tiered 2.0/3.0pt), and pattern_mid_conf (found,
   on inspection, to genuinely conflate two different dexter code paths worth
   different points — 1.0 vs 1.5 — that the label alone can't distinguish).
   fib_382 and fib_236 turned out to be dead tokens: dexter's fib engine only
   ever computes 50%/61.8%/65%/78.6%, never those two ratios.
5. No values were applied to dexter.py's real CONFLUENCE_SCORES — this phase
   only taught the proposal script what "current" means so it can print
   proposals. Every actual weight change still requires Kev to read the
   report and manually edit dexter.py himself.

VERIFICATION: `python -X utf8 weight_proposal.py --selftest` → 3/3 PASS.
`python -X utf8 weight_proposal.py` run against the real labels_closed.jsonl
(13,925 records read, 11,395 used) → weight_proposal_report.txt now shows a
real CUR_W number for all 29 mapped tags and a capped ±1 PROPOSAL for the 7
that are both mapped and statistically significant (gp -1, oi_confirm -1,
bb_mid -1, pattern_breakout -1, fast_anchor_pdl -1, bb_squeeze -1,
oi_divergence +1, fib_50 +1). Nothing in dexter.py, labeller.py, or any live
data file was touched — read-only investigation plus one edit to
weight_proposal.py's own CURRENT_WEIGHTS dict.

   _calc_confluence_score() (Chev's own manually-typed tag string scoring) —
   a different mechanism from the automatic per-scan Golden Pocket bonus
   that actually produced the -0.33R shadow evidence (a hardcoded
   "fib_score = 3" line in scan_pair_tf() that never reads
   CONFLUENCE_SCORES). Editing the dict key would not change the behavior

   inherited from the pre-existing WEIGHT_LAB_VERIFIED_TAGS "same

   contradicts.

   derivs.py's classify_derivs(), not dexter.py — out of this phase's
   stated dexter.py-only scope.
3. fib_50 (2->3): shares one code branch with fib_618 (not approved for
   change) — "if name in (\"50%\", \"61.8% (golden pocket)\"): fib_score +=
   2" scores both tags identically. Raising fib_50 alone requires splitting
   this into two branches, a logic change, not a number change.
4. fast_anchor_pdl (0->-1) and bb_squeeze (0->-1): as already flagged in
   Phase 2, neither has an existing scoring line — both are pure 0pt

=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT RECALIBRATION PHASE 3 (continued): 5 more of the 6 previously-skipped items resolved and applied — RESTART: REQUIRED, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: after the initial Phase 3 pass (2 applied, 6 skipped/flagged), Kev
gave explicit per-item decisions on the 6 open questions. 5 were approved for
implementation, 1 (fast_anchor_pdl/bb_squeeze new scoring logic) was declined
and left exactly as-is.

APPLIED THIS ROUND:
1. gp (real mechanism, 3->2): dexter.py scan_pair_tf() ~line 8925-8934 — the
   golden-pocket override that used to read "if in_golden_pocket and
   fib_score < 3: fib_score = 3" now reads "if in_golden_pocket: fib_score =
   2". CONFLUENCE_SCORES["gp"]=4 (Chev's manual-tag dict) was deliberately
   left untouched per Kev's choice — only the automatic scan mechanism moved.
2. fib_50 (2->3, fib_618 unchanged at 2): dexter.py ~line 8914-8920 — split
   the shared "if name in ('50%','61.8%...'): fib_score += 2" branch into a
   per-name point value (_fib_pts = 3 if name=='50%' else 2) so fib_50 and
   fib_618 can move independently.
3. IMPORTANT INTERACTION FOUND while combining #1 and #2: the old
   golden-pocket guard ("fib_score < 3") was only ever a no-op that happened
   to always be true under the single old shared value of 2. Once fib_50
   could independently reach fib_score==3, a golden-pocket touch reached via
   the 50% level would sit at 3 already and silently skip that guard —
   never collapsing to the GP tag the way a 61.8%-reached touch still would.
   Fixed by making the override unconditional ("if in_golden_pocket:") since
   the golden-pocket signal is meant to supersede whichever individual fib
   level triggered it either way. Without this fix, applying gp and fib_50
   together exactly as separately ratified would have introduced a real,
   silent scoring bug.
4. oi_confirm (1.0->0.0) and oi_divergence (1.5->2.5): derivs.py
   classify_derivs() ~line 103-118 — all 4 branches updated (both
   OI-divergence branches to 2.5, both OI-confirmation branches to 0.0),
   including the point value shown in each reason string.

DECLINED (left as-is): fast_anchor_pdl and bb_squeeze remain pure 0pt
context/gate signals — Kev chose not to add new scoring logic for either.

VERIFICATION: `git diff -- dexter.py derivs.py` shows exactly the lines
described above changed, nothing else. `python -c "import ast;
ast.parse(open('dexter.py', encoding='utf-8').read());
ast.parse(open('derivs.py', encoding='utf-8').read())"` -> both parsed clean.
No thresholds, EXPLORATION_MODE, gauntlet values, or anything of Jane's
touched.

FULL LIST OF ALL WEIGHT RECALIBRATION CHANGES THIS PHASE (across both
rounds): pattern_breakout 2.0->1.0, bb_mid 1.0->0.0, gp (automatic mechanism)
3->2, fib_50 2->3 (fib_618 unchanged), oi_confirm 1.0->0.0, oi_divergence
1.5->2.5. fast_anchor_pdl and bb_squeeze intentionally left unscored.

*** PHASE 6A COMPLETE — ROUTE HARDCODED SCAN WEIGHTS THROUGH ONE

   so every reload recomputes from the pristine snapshot and never compounds.

   drive BOTH tables via a _WEIGHT_TABLES pair-list. An override tag applies
   to whichever table(s) it is a baseline key of; a tag in BOTH tables is
   applied to BOTH; a tag in neither is ignored with a logged warning. Same

BUGS FOUND AND FIXED:
1. gp NEVER ACTUALLY WIRED (most important finding): SCAN_WEIGHTS["gp"]=2
   existed in the table with a comment claiming it drove the golden-pocket
   override, but the code still did a hardcoded "fib_score = 2" literal --

   finding) would have silently ignored any future Weight Lab change. Fixed:
   now reads SCAN_WEIGHTS["gp"].
2. pattern_high_conf and pattern_mid_conf reintroduce an ambiguity Phase 1
   deliberately excluded: scan_pair_tf's pattern branch has a third,
   unmigrated "elif volume_confirmed: pattern_score = 1.5" path that
   labeller.py's tokenizer cannot distinguish from either label.
   pattern_mid_conf's two real paths already disagree today (1.0 vs 1.5);
   pattern_high_conf's two paths merely coincide today (1.5 == 1.5), masking
   the same flaw until the first override changes one of them. Fixed:
   reverted both to their pre-6A hardcoded values, documented why in a new
   comment block, left them out of SCAN_WEIGHTS. pattern_breakout and
   pattern_breakout_vol were verified genuinely single-path/safe and remain
   migrated.
3. Stale reason-string text: several reason strings shown to Chev still
   hardcoded the point-value text (e.g. "0.5pt", "3pt", "0pt") instead of
   reading the live SCAN_WEIGHTS value -- meaning the moment any of these
   moved via a future override, Chev would be shown the OLD point value
   while the NEW value silently drove the real score. Fixed in dexter.py:
   rsi_ob, rsi_os, sweep, bb_near (x2), bb_mid. Fixed in derivs.py:
   oi_divergence (x2), oi_confirm (x2) -- computed the live value into a
   local variable once per branch, used in both the score and the string.
4. fib_382 and fib_236 were included in SCAN_WEIGHTS as if real -- Phase 1
   already established dexter's fib engine never computes those two ratios
   (only 50%/61.8%/65%/78.6% exist), so they were dead keys nothing ever
   read. Removed entirely. fib_786 is real but not independently wired (it
   shares fib_other's code branch) -- kept as a documented placeholder with
   a comment explaining a future split would be needed to make it
   independently adjustable.
5. Found and fixed an UNRELATED pre-existing bug while touching derivs.py:
   its own bottom-of-file self-test still asserted the PRE-Phase-3 point
   values (1.5/1.0) for oi_divergence/oi_confirm, five tests failing, since
   Phase 3's recalibration (1.5->2.5, 1.0->0.0) was never reflected there.
   Corrected the expected values; derivs.py now passes 12/12 self-tests
   (was 7/12 before this fix).

CONFLUENCE_SCORES (=4, Chev's manually-typed tag scoring) and SCAN_WEIGHTS

=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT RECALIBRATION PHASE 6D PART 1: friendly names everywhere + strategy snapshot panel — RESTART: NOT REQUIRED (frontend-only), DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: presentation-only pass on webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js. Read the file
first and reported two findings before editing (mandatory checkpoint):

1. The phase asked for a new hardcoded TAG_LABELS dictionary, but
   weight-lab.js already calls friendlyTag() (webapp/js/ui/watchlist.js),
   backed by a real server endpoint (/api/tag_registry -> dexter.py's
   TAG_REGISTRY, ~line 3007) that already has an entry -- name AND
   tooltip/definition -- for every one of the 19 verified tags. Building a
   second hardcoded dict would have recreated a two-sources-of-truth problem
   this whole build has been curing at every other layer. Kev's call: reuse
   the existing registry, add only the missing "raw code in small muted
   text" visual (the actual gap), never a parallel dictionary.
2. The phase named CSS variables (--bg-success, --text-success, --bg-danger,
   --text-danger, --text-muted) that don't exist anywhere in this codebase --
   confirmed by grep across webapp/css. Using them literally would render no
   color at all, silently. Kev's call: use the app's real, already-
   established convention instead (.tBull #089981 green / .tBear #f23645 red
   from toasts.css, var(--txt3) muted -- both already used throughout this
   exact file). Standing rule going forward: when phase text and the
   codebase's own conventions conflict, the codebase wins -- flag it, follow
   the convention.

CHANGES:
1. New shared _wlTagLabel(tag, inline) helper -- friendly name (via
   friendlyTag()) plus the raw tag code in 9.5px var(--txt3), inline or
   stacked. Applied everywhere a tag renders that didn't already show the
   raw code: proposal cards (added a code line beneath the one-liner,
   replacing the old title-tooltip-only treatment), the watching section,
   the pending-overrides banner, and the digest header's table rows. The
   manual editor's tag list already showed the raw code in parens -- left
   as-is, already compliant.
2. New _wlSnapshotPanel(proposals) -- "Strategy snapshot — what the weights
   currently say," rendered at the very top of the panel (above the
   pending-overrides banner, last_reviewed_at line, digest header, and
   cards). One row per verified-mapping tag: friendly name + raw code,
   horizontal bar sized by current_weight (largest positive weight = full
   width; zero/negative weights get a fixed minimal bar so they're still
   visible), current_weight as text, and a status word -- "earning"
   (significant, coef>0), "costing" (significant, coef<0), "unproven"
   (not yet significant) -- colored green/red/muted per finding 2 above.
   Renders from the fresh payload normally; during a freeze, falls back to
   the cached payload (see fix below); shows a one-line "snapshot appears
   after the first analysis" note if neither exists yet.
3. REQUIRED FIX to existing logic, not just an addition: the line caching
   proposals for the manual editor's FYI line ("if (prop.ok)
   _wlLastProposalPayload = prop.proposals || []") ran on EVERY successful
   response, including a frozen one -- whose own "proposals" field is always
   []. That meant the very first frozen load would silently wipe out
   whatever real snapshot was cached before the freeze started, defeating
   the fallback before it could ever be used. Changed the condition to
   "prop.ok && !prop.frozen" so the cache only updates from real data and
   survives untouched through any freeze window. Strictly more robust for
   the manual editor's existing FYI line too, not just the new panel.

Approve/revert/batch/manual request logic, endpoints, and index.html are
completely untouched -- confirmed by diff (only weight-lab.js in the
changed-files list).
