=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT RECALIBRATION PHASE 6D PART 2: freeze countdown with a time estimate — RESTART: NOT REQUIRED (frontend-only), DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: presentation-only pass on webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js, zero-backend
solution as the phase asked -- confirmed by re-reading _build_weight_proposal_
payload() that records_since_last_change/needed/frozen_since (already used
since 6C) are the only fields needed; no new backend field required.

One note on the verification step as written: this panel has no
auto-refresh (by design -- first-open + manual refresh-button only, per the
file's own header comment, specifically so a background refresh can never
land mid-edit). "Two auto-refreshes" in the phase text means two manual
clicks of the refresh icon in practice; the estimate logic itself doesn't
care how the check-ins happen, only that real wall-clock time passed between
them.

CHANGES:
1. New in-memory sample buffer (_wlFreezeSamples, capped at 6, no
   localStorage) recording {timestamp, records_since_last_change} on every
   frozen response. Buffer resets whenever frozen_since changes (a new
   freeze window started), so a stale rate from a PREVIOUS freeze can never
   leak into a new one's estimate.
2. _wlFreezeEtaText(): computes records/minute from the oldest vs newest
   sample in the buffer (smooths over one noisy refresh-to-refresh gap
   rather than reacting to just the last two check-ins). Returns '' (no
   estimate rendered at all) whenever the math isn't trustworthy: fewer than
   2 samples, zero/negative elapsed time, or a zero/negative record delta --
   never a placeholder guess dressed as a real number. Friendly units: "~N
   min to go" under 90 minutes, "~N hr to go" (one decimal under 10 hours)
   otherwise.
3. _wlFreezeBanner(): replaces the plain count line from 6C with a progress
   bar (records_since_last_change/needed, capped 0-100%) plus the existing
   count text, frozen_since (kept from 6C), and the ETA text when available.

Approve/revert/batch/manual request logic, endpoints, and index.html
untouched -- confirmed by diff (only weight-lab.js in the changed-files
list).

VERIFICATION: `node --check webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js` -> syntax OK.
Additionally ran a standalone Node simulation (not committed) mocking
Date.now() across 6 scenarios -- single sample (no estimate), a normal
positive-rate case (correct minute estimate), near-completion (rounds to a
minimum of 1 min, never 0 or negative), a slow-rate case (correctly switches
to hour units past the 90-minute threshold), a freeze-window change
(buffer correctly resets, no stale contamination), and a zero-delta case (no
estimate, not a fake "infinite time" guess) -- all 6 passed. `git diff --stat`
confirms only weight-lab.js changed, index.html and weight-lab.css untouched.
Kev still needs to confirm live: watch the banner across two manual
refreshes and confirm an estimate appears on the second (not verified here --

=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT RECALIBRATION PHASE 6D PART 3: change history with honest verdicts — RESTART: REQUIRED (new backend route), DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: the one backend part of Phase 6D. Reported the plan (route name,
data read, confirmation it mutates nothing) before writing any code, per the
mandatory checkpoint, and got go-ahead first.

BACKEND (dexter.py):
1. New GET /api/weight_history (no @require_key, matches /api/weight_proposal's
   own read-only pattern). New _weight_history_cache dict, same 300s
   (WEIGHT_PROPOSAL_CACHE_SECS) pattern as the existing proposal cache.
2. _build_weight_history_payload(): turns weight_overrides.json into a
   timeline with a before/after verdict per entry. Reuses
   weight_proposal.load_records()/prepare_sample()/net_r() -- the SAME
   filtering (POST-excluded, non-null realized_R) and cost handling the
   Ridge regression itself already uses, no second methodology invented, no
   new imports. Win rate uses labeller.py's own label==1 definition,
   replicated inline (2 lines) rather than a private cross-module call.
   Before = up to 2000 most recent records prior to the entry's applied_at
   (approved_at fallback); after = everything since, uncapped.
   verdict_status = "too_early" when n_after < FREEZE_MIN_RECORDS (the
   existing 200 constant, not a new magic number), else "ready" -- the
   after-stats are always computed and returned, but the frontend only
   renders them as a verdict when status is "ready".
3. CHECKED BEFORE WRITING ANYTHING, per the phase's own instruction:
   /api/weight_proposal/revert does entries.pop(idx) with NO tombstone left
   behind -- weight_overrides.json cannot record removals at all. Documented
   this in the payload's own removals_note field; reverted changes simply
   cannot appear in this history, nothing to reconstruct.
4. Malformed-entry handling: each entry validated (tag non-empty string,
   delta numeric, applied_at/approved_at present and parseable) before use;
   any failure increments malformed_entries and is skipped, never raises.
5. Writes nothing -- confirmed by diff (no _atomic_write_json or open(...,'w')
   call anywhere in the new code; only the docstrings mention "writes
   nothing").

FRONTEND (webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js only):
1. New "Change history" section at the bottom of the panel, appended on
   every reachable path (error/frozen/normal) -- it's Kev's record of what
   happened, independent of whether today's regression run succeeded.
   Fetched INDEPENDENTLY of the main proposal/overrides Promise.all so a
   hiccup on this one endpoint can never take down the core proposal-cards
   experience.
2. Entry line: "<date> — <label> <old>pt -> <new>pt · <source>" using
   _wlTagLabel (Part 1's shared helper, not a new dictionary) and
   "ratified by you" + raw source word for weight_lab/manual sources.
   old/new derived from the tag's live current_weight (already in the
   fetched /api/weight_proposal payload) minus this entry's delta -- but
   ONLY when this is the tag's sole entry in the whole timeline; with 2+
   entries for the same tag, intermediate historical values can't be safely
   reconstructed from current_weight alone, so those fall back to showing
   just the delta, exactly as the phase's own escape hatch allows.
3. Verdict line: "Since then: win rate X% (was Y%)" when verdict_status is
   "ready"; exactly "too early to judge (N of 200 records)" otherwise --
   the too_early gate is enforced by rendering choice here, matching the
   backend's own gate, never overridden client-side.
4. delta=0 markers render as one muted line ("<date> — marker: <evidence
   note>") with no verdict block, per spec.

1. trades_today: count of journal entries closed today (by ts date) plus
   open_trades opened today (by open_ts date). Read-only, wrapped in
   try/except, never raises.

   the freshest playbook file's age in seconds. Reuses the existing _age()
   helper verbatim, no new file-reading mechanism.

=== 2026-07-13 — WEIGHT LAB APPROVE BUTTON: root-caused and fixed "nothing happens" — RESTART: NOT REQUIRED (frontend-only), DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: Kev reported clicking Approve -1 in the Weight Lab did nothing --
popup confirmed, closed, button stayed yellow/active, and he'd clicked twice
worried about a double -2 application. Verified first (before touching
anything): read weight_overrides.json directly -- confirmed NOTHING had
been applied, not once, so no real weight was ever changed. Then asked Kev
to check the browser console; he found the real signal: `POST .../api/
weight_proposal/approve 400 (Bad Request)`, with zero on-page message at
all (not even an error). Restarting Dexter did not change the 400.

ROOT CAUSE #1 (the actual "invisible" bug): every Weight Lab success/error
message went through chat.js's _showToast(), which writes into
#analysisToast -- a chart-view element at z-index:150, positioned for the
main chart, not this panel. #strategyOverlay (the whole Strategy Dashboard,
including Weight Lab) sits at z-index:9999 and covers the full screen. Every
message -- success AND failure -- was firing correctly this entire time and
being 100% invisible, hidden behind the panel. This is why nothing appeared
to happen even on a genuinely successful approve, and why the 400 error
produced no visible feedback either.

FIX #1: added _wlShowMessage(kind, html) -- Weight Lab's own on-page message,
appended fresh to document.body at z-index:10000 (same proven above-the-
overlay pattern _wlShowConfirm's own modal already used, just a top-center
banner instead of a full modal, so it's guaranteed visible regardless of
what else is open). Replaced all 11 _showToast(...) call sites in
weight-lab.js (approve, approve-all, mark-reviewed, undo, manual-set, and
the preview/confirm error paths) with this.

ROOT CAUSE #2 (why the button still looked "active" even on a real success,
found while designing the fix, not yet directly confirmed as tonight's 400's
cause but a real bug regardless): /api/weight_proposal has its own 300-
second server-side cache. Right after a genuinely successful approve, the
very next load can still serve the OLD proposal payload -- same tag, same
proposed_delta, same "actionable" card -- looking exactly as clickable as
before. /api/weight_overrides, by contrast, is never cached and always
accurate.

FIX #2 (two layers): (a) instant client-side feedback -- on a successful
single approve, _wlApprove now immediately greys out and relabels that
specific card ("✓ QUEUED") before the reload even starts, no waiting on
network round-trips; (b) the real, comprehensive fix -- loadWeightLab now
cross-references the always-fresh /api/weight_overrides entries and
excludes ANY tag that already has an entry (pending or applied) from both
the actionable and watching lists, so a stale proposal payload can never
render a live-looking Approve button for a tag that dexter.py's own
_validate_weight_approval would reject anyway ("a pending override already
exists"). This covers every load path, not just the one card just clicked --
including a plain page refresh.

ALSO FOUND while bumping cache-bust: weight-lab.js's own version string
(20260713-1) had NEVER been bumped despite every Phase 6C/6D edit made to
this file earlier today -- meaning the browser could have been running a
stale, partially-updated copy of this file this entire time, independent of
the two bugs above. Bumped to 20260713-2.

STILL OPEN: the specific 400 rejection reason for Kev's actual click tonight
was never captured (the error text itself was invisible before this fix, and
he hasn't re-tried since). Once he reloads with this fix live, any future
rejection will show its real reason on-screen -- if it happens again, that
message will say exactly why (unverified mapping, no longer significant,
pending override already exists, etc.) rather than requiring another round
of guessing.

VERIFICATION: `node --check webapp/js/ui/weight-lab.js` -> syntax OK. `git
diff --stat` shows only weight-lab.js and index.html (cache-bust line)
changed. Cache-bust bumped: weight-lab.js 20260713-1 -> -2.
NOT independently verified live this session. Kev should hard refresh and
try Approve again -- if it fails, the actual reason will now be visible
on-screen; if it succeeds, the card should grey out immediately and stay
that way on reload.

RESTART: NOT REQUIRED -- frontend-only. DEPLOY: NO. RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

=== 2026-07-13 — CIRCUIT BREAKER made EXPLORATION_MODE-aware — RESTART: REQUIRED, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ===

CONTEXT: Kev saw a Telegram alert that the daily circuit breaker had tripped
(no new trades escalating) and wanted this fixed for EXPLORATION_MODE paper
trading specifically -- "let Chev get in as many trades as possible, as long
as he thinks it's a good setup." Investigated before touching anything:
honest_sim.py's DAILY_R_HALT = -3.0 is a single, mode-blind threshold --
today's real daily_risk.json showed daily_R = -3.59, confirming this was a
genuine trip, not a glitch. Crucially, this breaker had NEVER been hooked
into risk_gauntlet.py's existing, deliberate EXPLORATION_MODE/NORMAL profile
split ("one flag drives the whole risk posture," already used for R:R/heat/
concurrency caps) -- it was simply overlooked when that pattern was built.

DECISION (Kev's explicit calls, not assumed): keep a real backstop in
EXPLORATION_MODE rather than disabling the breaker entirely (in case
something is genuinely broken, not just a normal bad streak), specifically
at daily_R <= -6.0; NORMAL mode (EXPLORATION_MODE off) keeps the original
-3.0 unchanged.

CHANGES:

2026-07-13 -- Weight Preview vocabulary-mismatch fix (EMA 13 "no change"
suggestion) + combo-leaderboard text truncation fix
================================================================================

CONTEXT: Kev asked (with the Shadow Tag/Combo Leaderboard screenshots) why
the Weight Lab was suggesting EMA 13 go from 0.5 to 0.5 -- a proposal with
no actual change, yet still asking for approval -- and separately flagged
that combo names in the Shadow Combo Leaderboard get cut off mid-text.

ROOT CAUSE (Weight Lab): _preview_weight_change() (dexter.py ~line 1108),
which backs /api/weight_preview (the CONFIRM-popup dry-run), was never
updated when SCAN_WEIGHTS/WEIGHT_LAB_VERIFIED_TAGS grew from 3 tags to 19
during Phase 6A/6B -- it only ever checked _CONFLUENCE_BASELINE/
CONFLUENCE_SCORES. CONFLUENCE_SCORES uses the OLD, Chev-manual-tag
vocabulary ("ema_13", underscored) -- it has no "ema13" key at all (that's
SCAN_WEIGHTS's, the labeller.py scan-vocabulary name). So confirming an
approval for EMA 13 (or 15 of the other 19 verified tags -- everything
except gp/rsi_ob/rsi_os) should hit a 400 "not a known tag" error at the
CONFIRM step, not silently show "0.5 -> 0.5" -- this matches Kev's earlier
report the same night of a red 400 error appearing at Confirm. Either way,
the bug is real and blocks approving any of these 16 tags correctly.

FIX: _preview_weight_change() now checks SCAN_WEIGHTS/_SCAN_WEIGHTS_BASELINE
FIRST, falling back to CONFLUENCE_SCORES/_CONFLUENCE_BASELINE -- same
precedence _build_weight_proposal_payload() and _reload_weight_overrides()
already use ("SCAN_WEIGHTS is what the shadow-ledger evidence actually
measures"). The 400 error message also now names both tables instead of
just CONFLUENCE_SCORES. NO weight VALUES changed -- this restores intended
approval behavior for tags that were already supposed to work per Phase 6B,
it does not add or alter any weight.

ROOT CAUSE (combo truncation): .stratBarLabel (strategy.css ~line 516) is a
shared 170px/ellipsis rule used by every leaderboard row (single-tag AND
combo). Combo names ("EMA 13 + EMA 21 + Sweep") run far longer than single
tag names and were getting clipped mid-combo.

FIX: added a scoped override -- #stratShadowComboBars .stratBarLabel and
#stratComboBars .stratBarLabel (the real closed-trade combo leaderboard has
the identical bug once it has enough data, same rendering pattern, so fixed
both) now get width:230px and wrap onto multiple lines instead of
ellipsis-clipping. Single-tag leaderboards are untouched (still 170px/
ellipsis, unchanged).

Also answered (no code change): Kev's "EMA 13 + EMA 21 + EMA 55 is
basically the same indicator" observation about misleading combos, whether
Liquidity Sweep is already implemented (yes -- SCAN_WEIGHTS["sweep"]=3,
already live), why Chev keeps skipping on "invalidation too close to
entry" (noise-floor / stop-distance explanation, not a "closeness to a
level is bullish" read), and whether an automatic shadow-to-weights
pipeline exists (no -- Weight Lab's Ridge regression is the closest

2026-07-14 -- PHASE 1 of 3: consolidate the weight-table lookup logic
(architecture cleanup requested after the "honest assessment" conversation)
================================================================================

CONTEXT: Kev asked me (Lead AI Quant Strategist hat) to fix 3 things I'd
criticized: (1) two overlapping confluence-weight tables causing repeated
bugs, (2) Chev's skip reasoning being free-text-only with no stable
category, (3) the Weight Lab's freeze window being global instead of
per-tag. Explicit instructions: don't assume anything, read handoff.txt,
search the code, verify nothing breaks, keep the strategy safe.

IMPORTANT REVERSAL, found via deep research (2 parallel Explore agents +
direct code/data reads) BEFORE touching any code: two of my three original
diagnoses were wrong, and I told Kev so before proceeding.

- CONFLUENCE_SCORES is NOT a redundant duplicate of SCAN_WEIGHTS. It's dead
  everywhere except 2 read-only display endpoints and one zero-caller
  function (_calc_confluence_score) -- EXCEPT it is also the exact
  vocabulary all 131 real historical trades in chev_journal.json are
  tagged with (confirmed by directly sampling the file: entries like
  "sr_4h,fib_1h,gp,dv,ema_55,ema_21,ema_13,bbsq,rsi_form_1h"). SCAN_WEIGHTS
  is the live vocabulary driving scan_pair_tf(), Chev's real prompt, and
  the real escalation gate. These are two legitimately different,
  both-still-needed vocabularies (live scan vs. historical journal
  tagging) -- merging the DATA would risk breaking real historical
  trade-tag display. Kev agreed: don't merge the tables.
- The Weight Lab's freeze window is NOT a design flaw. weight_proposal.py's
  Ridge regression fits ALL tags in ONE joint multivariate design matrix
  (build_design_matrix/ridge_fit) -- coefficients are not independent per
  tag. Changing any one tag's live weight changes scan_pair_tf()'s total
  score, which changes which setups get escalated/recorded for EVERY tag
  going forward, not just the changed one. A per-tag freeze window would
  let the regression mix data from different selection regimes -- it
  would be statistically unsound, not an improvement. Kev agreed: no
  structural change to the freeze window (see Phase 3 entry, still to
  come, for the write-up).

WHAT WAS ACTUALLY WRONG (and is what this phase fixes): the "check
SCAN_WEIGHTS first, fall back to CONFLUENCE_SCORES" rule was independently
re-implemented in THREE places (_build_weight_proposal_payload,
_preview_weight_change, _validate_weight_approval) instead of living in
one place. One of those three copies drifting out of sync is exactly how
yesterday's _preview_weight_change bug happened.

FIX: new pure helper _resolve_weight_tag(tag) added at dexter.py ~line 2971
(right after _SCAN_WEIGHTS_BASELINE is defined) -- single source of truth
returning {"baseline":..., "current":...} with SCAN_WEIGHTS-first
precedence, or None if the tag is in neither table. All three call sites
now delegate to it instead of re-implementing the check:
  - _build_weight_proposal_payload's current_weight lookup (~line 934-940)
  - _preview_weight_change's baseline/current_effective lookup (~line 1108)
  - _validate_weight_approval's "is this tag known" check (~line 1022)

EXPLICITLY NOT TOUCHED: _reload_weight_overrides()'s _WEIGHT_TABLES apply
loop -- it correctly applies a delta to EVERY table containing the tag
(gp/rsi_ob/rsi_os live in both), which is different semantics from "resolve
one display value" and was never a source of any bug. Also not touched:
/api/weight_manual's editor route (~line 1249) -- it's deliberately scoped
to CONFLUENCE_SCORES only (Kev's manual override editor for the legacy
vocabulary specifically), not one of the three drifting copies.

VERIFICATION: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('dexter.py',
encoding='utf-8').read())"` -> OK. Manual trace of all three refactored
call sites against their prior inline logic confirms byte-identical
behavior for the 3 shared tags (gp/rsi_ob/rsi_os) and the 16 SCAN_WEIGHTS-
only verified tags. Grepped for any remaining inline duplicate of the old
pattern -- none found outside the untouched routes named above. No
dexter.py execution (never run the bot).

RESTART: REQUIRED for this refactor to take effect. DEPLOY: NO.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

2026-07-14 -- PHASE 2 of 3: structured reject codes (additive, analytics-only)
================================================================================

CONTEXT: second of the 3 issues from the "honest assessment" -- Chev's own
skip/reject reasoning was free-text only (3,082 distinct strings across
4,981 SKIPs, confirmed by direct frequency count), making trend questions
like "why does Chev keep skipping on X" require an ad hoc grep instead of a
real number. Separately, risk_gauntlet.py's gate rejections already compute
a stable reject_code (ATR_FLOOR, NET_RR, COST_GATE, ... 12 codes total) but
it was silently discarded before logging.

2a. STOP DISCARDING THE GATE'S OWN REJECT_CODE. _log_chev_decision()
(dexter.py ~line 4129) gained one new optional kwarg reject_code=None,
added to the logged entry dict -- same additive-field pattern as the
existing ev_advisory_rr/enforced_rr_floor params (old log lines simply
won't have it). Both risk_gauntlet REJECT call sites (~13756 and ~13767)
already had _g_rc in scope and now pass reject_code=_g_rc. Only affects NEW
records going forward -- it's a log field, not a gate input, so this cannot
change any trading decision. The other REJECT-family decisions
(GATE_REJECT/STRUCT_REJECT/MTF_TAX_REJECT/HALLUCINATED_LEVELS) were NOT
touched -- their `decision` value already IS a stable code by itself

before /api/strategy/funnel ~line 582) buckets Chev's own SKIP free-text
into 9 stable categories: INVALIDATION_TOO_CLOSE, INVALIDATION_MISSING,

CONFIRMATION_MISSING, STRUCTURAL_SUPPORT_MISSING, TREND_CONTEXT, OTHER.
Same ordered-substring-check style as counterfactual_report.py's existing
classify_reject_reason(). RISK_REWARD_OR_SIZING was NOT in the original
plan -- added after testing against real data showed it's a genuinely
large, distinct category (~18% of all skips: R:R/round-trip-cost/ATR-floor
language), not noise. Never touches Chev's prompt or parse_chev_reply() --
purely a post-hoc read of the already-logged reason string, analytics only.

0.9%, OTHER 8.5% -- manually eyeballed the top 25 OTHER examples twice
(iterating the category rules once) to confirm nothing large or coherent
was being missed; the remaining OTHER residual is genuinely miscellaneous

2026-07-14 -- PHASE 3 of 3: freeze-window review -- NO CODE CHANGE
================================================================================

CONTEXT: third of the 3 issues from the "honest assessment" -- the Weight
Lab's freeze window (_build_weight_proposal_payload, dexter.py) computes
ONE global freeze_epoch from the most recent applied_at/approved_at across
ALL entries in weight_overrides.json, then requires FREEZE_MIN_RECORDS=200
fresh records before ANY tag gets a new proposal. This looked, from the
outside, like it should be scoped per-tag instead -- approving one small
change to one tag currently freezes proposals for every OTHER tag too,
which reads as an unnecessary slowdown.

RESEARCH FINDING (before writing any code, per Kev's explicit "don't
assume, verify" instruction): this is NOT a design flaw, and a per-tag
freeze window would actually make the statistics worse, not better. Two
independent reasons, both confirmed by reading weight_proposal.py in full:

1. build_design_matrix()/ridge_fit() fit ALL tags in ONE joint multivariate
   regression over a single design matrix (one X, one y, one beta vector).
   Tag coefficients are NOT independent -- each tag's fitted coefficient is
   conditional on every other tag's column in the SAME fit. Bootstrap CIs
   refit the full joint model per resample too. There is no mechanism in
   ridge_fit for "tag A uses rows 1-500, tag B uses rows 200-700 of the
   same regression" -- a per-tag freeze window isn't something the current
   math could even express, let alone safely.
2. More fundamentally: changing ANY tag's live weight changes
   scan_pair_tf()'s total_score, which is the number that decides which
   setups get escalated to Chev and recorded to labels_closed.jsonl in the
   first place. So a weight change to tag A shifts the SELECTION of which
   setups show up in the shadow ledger for EVERY tag going forward, not
   just tag A. A per-tag freeze would let the regression silently mix
   evidence drawn from two different selection regimes for other tags --
   exactly the kind of contamination the freeze window exists to prevent.
   The global scope is the correct scope, not a limitation of it.

DECISION (Kev, in-session): no structural change. This finding was
presented plainly (including that it reversed my own earlier stated
opinion) before any code was touched, alongside the parallel finding that
Issue 1 (CONFLUENCE_SCORES vs SCAN_WEIGHTS) also wasn't what it first
looked like -- see the PHASE 1 entry above for that one. Recorded here so
this doesn't get re-flagged as an unfixed bug in a future session.

NO FILES TOUCHED. NO VERIFICATION NEEDED. RESTART: N/A. DEPLOY: N/A.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

================================================================================
This closes out all 3 items from the "honest assessment" conversation:
  Issue 1 (weight-table duplication)  -> fixed via lookup consolidation (Phase 1)
  Issue 2 (no structured reject codes) -> fixed, additive + retroactive (Phase 2)
  Issue 3 (global freeze window)       -> reviewed, correct as designed (Phase 3)

2026-07-14 -- "SECOND LOOK" FIX ROUND, PHASE 1 of 5: chev_journal.json race +
non-atomic write
================================================================================

CONTEXT: Kev asked for a further "what else needs a second look" pass. I
researched 3 angles (dead/discarded code, duplicated logic across files,
concurrency safety) and reported 7 candidates in plain English. Kev asked
to fix all of them -- same explicit instructions as the last round: don't
assume, verify directly, ask if unsure, keep the strategy safe.

BEFORE writing any code this round, I re-verified all 7 candidates against
the LIVE code (not the earlier summarized research). Two turned out to be
non-issues -- see the PHASE 4 entry (still to come) for the full writeup:
COST_R_CAP's 3-way duplication is explicitly documented in all three files
as "by design... stays standalone," not an accident; the frontend
"Volume Profile vs Vol Profile" thing turned out to be two intentionally
different registries (full name vs. compact chip label) and, separately,
two entirely unrelated features that happen to share a 2-letter code
(a confluence tag vs. a chart-drawing-tool button) -- not real
inconsistencies once traced to their actual call sites.

PROBLEM (verified real): chev_journal.json -- the real trade history file
everything else (Weight Lab, win-rate stats, Learn tab) depends on -- had
NO lock and NO atomic write anywhere. 6 places write it: /api/close_trade
(Flask request thread, force-close), _do_postmortem (background thread),
and 4 partial-TP sites inside the main scan loop. Every one did
`journal = _load_journal()` -> mutate in memory -> plain `open(path,"w")`
+ `json.dump(...)`. Two writers reading the same "before" state at the
same instant (e.g. a manual force-close landing at the same moment as an
automatic partial-TP write) could silently clobber each other's addition,
and a crash mid-write could truncate the whole file (no temp-file+replace
like weight_overrides.json already gets via _atomic_write_json).

FIX: new `_JOURNAL_LOCK = threading.Lock()` and `_save_journal_atomic(data)`
(dexter.py, right after _load_journal(), ~line 4103) -- same temp-file +
os.replace pattern as the existing _atomic_write_json, journal-specific by
convention with _load_journal(). All 6 write sites now wrap their existing
load -> mutate -> write sequence in `with _JOURNAL_LOCK:` and call
_save_journal_atomic() instead of a raw open()/json.dump. No change to any
site's dedupe-check logic or what gets written -- purely wraps the
existing sequence. jane_journal.json is explicitly untouched (standing
rule) -- confirmed via grep that its own separate write path
(~line 11822) was not modified.

VERIFICATION: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('dexter.py',
encoding='utf-8').read())"` -> OK. Grepped for any remaining raw
`open(JOURNAL_PATH, "w")` -- none found, all 6 now go through
_save_journal_atomic. Confirmed exactly 6 call sites of
_save_journal_atomic (matching the 6 known write locations) and confirmed
jane_journal.json's own write path is untouched. No dexter.py execution
(never run the bot).

RESTART: REQUIRED for this to take effect. DEPLOY: NO.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

2026-07-14 -- "SECOND LOOK" FIX ROUND, PHASE 2 of 5: weight_overrides.json +
CONFLUENCE_SCORES/SCAN_WEIGHTS races
================================================================================

PROBLEM (verified): 6 Flask routes (approve, approve_batch, mark_reviewed,
weight_manual [2 write paths in one route], revert) and
_reload_weight_overrides() itself all did read-modify-write on
weight_overrides.json with no lock -- confirmed every span is fast, pure
in-memory work (no network/slow I/O between the read and the write at any
of them). Separately, _reload_weight_overrides() mutates the live
CONFLUENCE_SCORES/SCAN_WEIGHTS dicts key-by-key with no lock.

IMPORTANT SCOPE NARROWING (verified before writing code, not assumed): the
dict-mutation race is narrower than it first looked. _reload_weight_overrides()
and the scoring engine (scan_pair_tf) both only ever run on the background
scan-loop thread, confirmed by checking every call site of each -- they are
never concurrent with each other, so the hot live-scoring path was never
actually at risk. The real exposure is exactly 2 Flask GET routes that
iterate the FULL dict for one consistent snapshot: /api/weight_manual/tags
and /api/tag_registry. _resolve_weight_tag()'s single-key reads (used by
_build_weight_proposal_payload, _preview_weight_change,
_validate_weight_approval) don't need protection either -- a single dict
.get() can't return a torn/partial value regardless of threading.

FIX: one new `_WEIGHT_STATE_LOCK = threading.Lock()` (dexter.py, right after
WEIGHT_OVERRIDES_FILE's definition) covers BOTH the file and the in-memory
tables, since they're the same conceptual state (file = durable copy, dicts
= live cache). Wrapped in `with _WEIGHT_STATE_LOCK:`:
  - All 6 Flask route bodies' existing read -> modify -> _atomic_write_json
    span (api_weight_proposal_approve, approve_batch, mark_reviewed,
    weight_manual, revert) -- no change to any route's logic, purely wraps
    the existing sequence.
  - _reload_weight_overrides()'s entire body (its own file read, both
    CONFLUENCE_SCORES/SCAN_WEIGHTS mutation loops, and its conditional
    applied_at write-back) -- one lock now covers the file and the dicts
    together, which is what closes the dict-race too.
  - The two dict-iterating comprehensions inside api_weight_manual_tags and
    api_tag_registry (brief, read-only, no behavior change).
  - scan_pair_tf and every other single-key reader of CONFLUENCE_SCORES/
    SCAN_WEIGHTS deliberately left untouched (same-thread with the reload,
    or single-key-atomic -- not a real risk, and locking the hot scoring
    path would be needless overhead for zero safety gain).

VERIFICATION: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('dexter.py',
encoding='utf-8').read())"` -> OK. Counted _WEIGHT_STATE_LOCK usages (9 =
1 definition + 5 route/function wraps + 2 dict-reader wraps... plus the
reload function itself, matching the intended 8 wrap sites). Re-checked
every remaining unwrapped `_read_weight_overrides_file()` call site
(api_weight_overrides, _build_weight_history_payload,
build_elliot_suggestions, and the payload builder's own read) -- confirmed
each is genuinely read-only for this file (docstrings say so and no write
follows), so they're safe without the lock now that all writes are
atomic. No dexter.py execution (never run the bot).

RESTART: REQUIRED for this to take effect. DEPLOY: NO.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

================================================================================
2026-07-14 -- "SECOND LOOK" FIX ROUND, PHASE 3 of 5: stop hiding real
failures -- 3 silent scoring blocks + 1 discarded retry rejection reason
================================================================================

3a. THREE `except Exception: pass` BLOCKS IN THE LIVE SCORING PATH
(scan_pair_tf, which computes dexter_score -- the number that gates
escalation to Chev): chart pattern engine (~line 9434-9508, was
`except Exception as _pe: pass` -- the exception was already being
captured into a variable and then never used), Bollinger Band scoring
(~line 9477-9551), Volume Profile scoring (~line 9519-9591). If any of
these ever throws, that scoring component was silently contributing 0
with zero visibility -- indistinguishable from "this signal genuinely
wasn't present." Fixed to `except Exception as e: print(f"[Dexter] <block>
scoring failed for {symbol}/{primary_tf}: {e}")` -- still doesn't crash,
still zeroes out the score (NO behavior change to any trading decision),
just now visible in the console/logs if it ever actually happens.

(Note: ~37 other `except Exception: pass` blocks exist elsewhere in
dexter.py. Sampled a few during research -- they're lower-stakes,
cosmetic/logging paths, not scoring inputs. Auditing all 40 is a much
bigger, differently-scoped task nobody asked for; only these 3 confirmed
scoring-path ones were in scope this round.)

3b. GAUNTLET RETRY WAS DISCARDING ITS OWN REJECTION REASON (~line
13775-13840): when Chev revises a rejected trade and the gauntlet runs
again on the revision, if the revision was ALSO rejected, the code fell
through to the shared log call still using `_g_rc`/`_g_rr`/`_g_res` from
the ORIGINAL (pre-revision) rejection -- the retry's own
reject_code/reject_reason/cost_r/ev_advisory_rr/enforced_rr_floor were
computed into `_g_res2` and then never used. A trade revised for one
reason (e.g. ATR_FLOOR) that then failed for a completely different
reason on the retry (e.g. NET_RR) was logged as if it failed for the
first reason again.

FIX: added an `else` branch right after `if _g_res2["verdict"] == "PASS":`
that reassigns `_g_res = _g_res2`, `_g_rc = _g_res2["reject_code"]`,
`_g_rr = _g_res2["reject_reason"]` before falling through to the shared
log call -- this also fixes cost_r/ev_advisory_rr/enforced_rr_floor in
that same log line, which had the identical "still describes the original
attempt" problem since they're all read off `_g_res`. The PASS branch is
completely untouched.

VERIFICATION: `python -c "import ast; ast.parse(open('dexter.py',
encoding='utf-8').read())"` -> OK. Grepped to confirm all 4 fixes landed
exactly once each. Confirmed `symbol`/`primary_tf` (used in the 3 new
print statements) are real parameters of scan_pair_tf, in scope at each
except block. Confirmed the retry fix's reassignment happens before the
shared `_log_chev_decision(...)` call that reads `_g_res`/`_g_rc`/`_g_rr`.
No dexter.py execution (never run the bot).

RESTART: REQUIRED for this to take effect. DEPLOY: NO.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

*** PHASE R1 — TRENDLINE RAY EXTENSION FIX IN patterns.py — 2026-07-14 —
RESTART: YES (patterns.py imported by dexter.py), DEPLOY: NO (JS verification
is read-only), RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
================================================================================

CONTEXT: `_trendline_endpoints()` in patterns.py draws the upper/lower
boundary lines the webapp's "PAT" Arsenal tool renders (ascending/descending
triangles, wedges, channels). It accepts `n_extend_bars=25`, clearly intended
to project the line forward past the current candle so it behaves like a ray
rather than a segment that dead-ends at "now." One expression permanently
discarded that extension. This phase fixes only that one expression — the
trendline FIT math (_local_trendline, _global_trendline, pivot selection) is
untouched, as is the horizontal S/R system, per this build's hard rules.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:
1. patterns.py, `_trendline_endpoints()`: the line
     end_local = min(len(df_window) - 1 + n_extend_bars, len(df_window) - 1)
   always evaluated to the un-extended value, because len+n_extend_bars is
   always greater than len whenever n_extend_bars is positive — a min/max
   mixup, not a deliberate clamp. Changed to:
     end_local = len(df_window) - 1 + max(0, n_extend_bars)
   The future-timestamp estimation branch immediately below (bar_seconds
   extrapolation, ~line 457-461) was already correct and already guarded for
   len(df_window) < 2 — it had simply never executed. It now does. No other
   line in the function changed; the ts_end index-safety clamp
   (`min(end_local, len(df_window) - 1)` used only to read a safe placeholder
   timestamp before the extrapolation branch overwrites it) is a different
   expression from the bug and was left exactly as-is, per instruction.
2. test_ray_extension.py (new file, dexter.py root): offline self-test, no
   dexter import, no network — synthetic 30-bar hourly DataFrame with known
   slope/intercept, calls `_trendline_endpoints` directly. 7/7 checks pass:
   ray extends by exactly n_extend_bars*bar_seconds; p2 matches `_project()`
   at the extended bar index; n_extend_bars=0 reproduces the old (correct)
   un-extended behaviour exactly; t1/p1 unchanged by the fix either way.

BENEFIT: the trendline boundaries patterns.py already computes and already
narrates well (touch-tolerant, ATR-scaled, backtested) can now actually be
drawn as forward-looking rays instead of segments that stop at the current
candle — the prerequisite for treating a diagonal line as a live, moving
support/resistance reference rather than a historical artifact. This phase
is deliberately just the drawing-math fix; ray identity/persistence, trust
tallies, Chev narration, and mid-trade alert wiring are separate, later
phases and were NOT touched here.

CONSUMER AUDIT (Task 4): grepped dexter.py, chart_drawer.py, webapp/js for
every reader of upper_trendline/lower_trendline and the t1/p1/t2/p2 dict
shape. dexter.py's only reference is the None-fallback default in the empty
pattern result (~line 2574) — not a value consumer. chart_drawer.py has zero
references (Chev's manual draw_trend_line tool takes explicit coordinates
from Chev, unrelated code path). webapp/js/charts/engine.js reads
pat.upper_trendline/lower_trendline in three places (_drawPatternLine,
the "PAT ~" label, and the "no named pattern" fallback text) — all either
draw whatever t1/p1/t2/p2 they're given or just check truthiness, neither
assumes t2 equals the last candle. Separately confirmed breakout detection
in patterns.run() (breakout_up/breakout_dn) calls its OWN _project(...,
last_idx) before _trendline_endpoints is ever invoked — it does not consume
_trendline_endpoints' output at all, so breakout/pattern-selection behavior
is provably unaffected by this fix. One near-miss worth recording: chat.js
line ~674 (`time1: L.t1, price1: L.p1, time2: L.t2, price2: L.p2`) uses the
same field names but is a completely separate, self-contained client-side
trendline tool (the "TL" Arsenal layer / drawTrendlines()) that detects its
own pivots from currentCandles in the browser — it does not read patterns.py
output and is untouched either way. No consumer breaks under a future t2.

JS VERIFICATION (Task 5, read-only, no edits): webapp/js/charts/drawing.js's
timeToX() falls back to linear extrapolation (via _bm(), which reads the
pixel spacing between the last two candles) whenever the chart library's
native timeToCoordinate() returns null for an out-of-range timestamp — this
looks like it was built for the existing RSI forming-divergence 4-bar
projection. _bm() depends only on `currentCandles`, which chart-core.js
populates unconditionally whenever candle data loads — not gated by
_engineReadoutActive or the PAT tool's own state — so the fallback's
prerequisite is met in the PAT-only code path (patterns draw independently
of _engineReadoutActive per an existing code comment in engine.js).

VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile patterns.py test_ray_extension.py` ->
exit 0. `python test_ray_extension.py` -> 7/7 PASS. Existing self-tests
re-run to confirm no regression: `python -X utf8 derivs.py` -> 12/12 PASS
(unchanged from baseline); `python labeller.py` -> 26/26 PASS (unchanged).
Grep-confirmed the new line landed exactly once and the old min()-mixup
pattern no longer appears anywhere in patterns.py. No dexter.py execution,
bot never run.

REMAINING UNCERTAIN / MANUAL VERIFICATION NEEDED FROM KEV: this phase
proves the Python math and the JS extrapolation path exist and are wired

last candle, and (2) separately confirm an RSI forming-divergence projection
still renders as before. If the Python fix passes but lines don't visibly

*** PHASE R2 — RAY REGISTRY (PURE MODULE, NO WIRING) — 2026-07-14 —
RESTART: NO (new module, nothing imports it yet), DEPLOY: NO,
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
================================================================================

CONTEXT: patterns.py refits trendlines from scratch every scan (last-3-pivot
OLS) with no memory that "this specific line has been respected N times over
its life." This phase builds that memory as a standalone module, modeled on
derivs.py (constants at top with WHY comments, pure logic functions, offline
self-test under __main__). Nothing imports it yet — wiring is Phase R3+.
The trendline fit math, the horizontal S/R system, and SCAN_WEIGHTS/
WEIGHT_LAB_VERIFIED_TAGS were all read but not touched, per this build's
hard rules.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY: new file ray_registry.py (C:\ChevTools\). Implements,
exactly per the phase design and no more:
- RayRecord dataclass with the listed fields (id, symbol, timeframe, side,
  slope_raw/norm, anchor_ts, value_at_anchor, born_ts, last_seen_ts,
  lifetime_span_bars, respect_count, wick_rejection_count, state,
  last_break_ts, alerted_trade_ids) PLUS four internal bookkeeping fields
  not in the phase's listed set (touch_open, pending_break, first_touch_ts,
  last_touch_ts) — added because update_touches/update_break_state must
  persist state across separate calls (a touch or a pending break can span
  a call boundary) and the listed field set had nowhere to put it. Flagged
  clearly in the dataclass's own comment for whoever wires this in R3.
- reconcile(): the identity function. Same-line test is normalized-slope
  delta <= SLOPE_MATCH_TOL AND the EXISTING ray's own value projected
  forward to the new current bar within VALUE_MATCH_TOL_ATR x ATR of the
  new fit's value at that bar. Re-anchors to (current_bar_ts,
  value_at_current_bar) on every call (match or mint) rather than adopting
  patterns.py's own intercept convention — sidesteps the "intercept means a
  different bar index every refit" trap entirely, since this module never
  reads patterns.py's raw intercept, only slope + a value-at-a-known-time
  pair it defines itself. Retires LIVE rays idle >= RAY_STALE_BARS (own
  timeframe's bar count) BEFORE attempting a match. A non-match does NOT
  evict the old ray — it stays LIVE, a new one is minted alongside it; the
  >2-per-side cap is enforced later, at select_live() (render time), not
  here — the registry can remember more than it shows. NOTE: the phase's
  listed signature didn't include a registry argument; added one as an
  explicit parameter (matching derivs.py's style of explicit inputs over
  hidden module state) since reconcile() has nothing to reconcile against
  without it. Every decision (MATCHED/MINTED/RETIRED, with the numbers that
  drove it) is appended as one JSON line to ray_identity_log.jsonl.
- update_touches(): touch opens within TOUCH_TOL_ATR, stays open across
  hugging bars (counts once), closes on release (>= TOUCH_RELEASE_ATR away)
  or on a wick-through-and-reject (closes AND increments
  wick_rejection_count — a trap counts as evidence FOR the line). See
  SECOND-PASS REVIEW below for a same-bar edge case considered and
  deliberately NOT changed.
- update_break_state(): replicates patterns.py's _atr_breakout_pct formula
  (patterns.py ~line 59-68) rather than importing it, to keep this module
  standalone — same tradeoff labeller.py already accepts for its own local
  COST_R_CAP copy. BROKEN requires two CONSECUTIVE qualifying closes; one
  alone sets a persisted pending_break flag and leaves the ray LIVE; a
  non-qualifying follow-up resets the flag (a reclaim does not resurrect a
  BROKEN id — a later matching fit mints a fresh line with fresh tallies,
  per the phase's explicit instruction).
- horizon_bars(): direction always comes from the current local fit
  (untouched, lives in patterns.py); only REACH is earned by lifetime —
  lifetime_span_bars x 1/3, capped at 40 bars, floored at 5.
- time_to_cross(): pure, direction-aware (levels behind the ray's path are
  excluded), filtered to horizon_bars(). Takes a flat (price, label) list
  supplied by the caller — this function computes nothing about what those
  levels are, so adding a future static tool means only appending to that
  list, no change here.
- select_live(): per (symbol, timeframe, side) group, keeps at most
  MAX_LIVE_PER_SIDE=2 LIVE rays ranked by respect_count (r² tiebreak
  supplied by caller). A candidate is dropped as a near-duplicate only if
  BOTH its value is within DISTINCT_MIN_ATR x ATR of an already-kept ray's
  AND its slope is within SLOPE_MATCH_TOL — otherwise a distinct ray is
  kept even if a higher-ranked duplicate had to be dropped to make room for
  it. NOTE: extended beyond the phase's one-argument select_live(rays)
  signature to also take current_bar_ts and atr_by_key, since the
  described distinctness/ranking behavior is not computable without them.
- load_registry()/save_registry(): atomic write (temp file + os.replace),
  same crash-safe pattern as dexter.py's _atomic_write_json (dexter.py
  ~line 844), replicated rather than imported to keep this module
  standalone. Missing/corrupt file -> empty registry, warning printed,
  never raises.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,
re-reading the diff cold): the one real finding was in update_touches(). A
candidate improvement was drafted to also recognize a wick-through-and-
reject within a SINGLE bar (no prior bar having opened the touch) — e.g. a
one-candle stop-hunt spike that pierces the ray and snaps back. That draft
was rejected after tracing it through: without requiring a PRIOR bar to have
already registered "within tolerance," the same-bar check ("extreme beyond
tolerance on the wrong side, close on the correct side") would also fire on
any ordinary bar that has nothing to do with the ray at all — e.g. price
trading in a completely different range that scan, whose low happens to sit
far past the line while its unrelated close happens to land on the "correct"
side. That's a false positive, not a trap. The shipped version deliberately
requires touch_open to already be True (i.e., a previous bar was observed
within TOUCH_TOL_ATR) before a wick-through-and-reject can be recognized —
this means a genuine single-candle spike-and-reject with NO prior in-
tolerance bar is not currently counted. Traced every consumer this module
could affect: none, since it is not imported anywhere (confirmed by repo-
wide grep) — this review was entirely about correctness of the module's own
internal logic and forward-compatibility for R3's wiring, not about any
live blast radius. No fix applied because the SHIPPED code was already the
safe version; the flawed variant was never committed to the file.

VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile ray_registry.py` -> exit 0. New self-
test `python -X utf8 ray_registry.py` -> 21/21 PASS, covering: identity
match vs mint at both tolerance boundaries; a non-matching scan does NOT
evict the old ray; retire-on-stale (99 bars idle = not yet, 100 = retired);
hugging for 5 bars then releasing = exactly one respected touch; wick-
through-snap-back increments both respect_count and wick_rejection_count;
two-close break confirmation (one qualifying close alone stays LIVE with a
pending flag; a non-qualifying follow-up resets it; two CONSECUTIVE
qualifying closes -> BROKEN); horizon floor/growth/cap across a young, mid-
life, and old ray; time_to_cross excludes a level behind the ray's path and
one beyond its horizon, keeps the one within it; select_live drops a near-
duplicate ray in favor of keeping a lower-ranked-but-distinct one;
persistence round-trip; corrupt-file and missing-file recovery (both ->
empty registry, no exception). Existing self-tests re-run for regression
(expected unaffected, verified anyway per the floor): `python -X utf8
derivs.py` -> 12/12 PASS, `python labeller.py` -> 26/26 PASS, both unchanged.
Grep-confirmed zero imports of ray_registry anywhere in the repo. Confirmed
by design that running the self-test never touches the real
C:\ChevTools\ray_registry.json / ray_identity_log.jsonl production paths —
every test I/O path is redirected to a temp directory. No dexter.py
execution, bot never run.

REMAINING UNCERTAIN / FOR R3 TO DECIDE: (1) thread-safety — save_registry/
load_registry have no lock, unlike dexter.py's _lock around its own JSON
saves; a non-issue while nothing calls this module, but R3 must add locking
if reconcile()/save_registry() end up called from more than one thread
(Dexter's BOS-alert path already fires background threads) — deliberately
not designed here since the call pattern doesn't exist yet. (2) the same-
bar wick-reject gap documented above — worth watching in the real
ray_identity_log.jsonl once wired, to see how often a genuine single-candle
spike-and-reject gets missed in practice before deciding whether a safer,
range-aware version of that check is worth building. (3) reconcile()'s and
select_live()'s signatures both grew beyond the phase's literal one-line
form (a registry arg; current_bar_ts + atr_by_key) — necessary for the
described behavior, documented in-code and here, but worth double-checking
against whatever R3 was already planning to pass in.

RESTART: NO (new module, nothing imports it yet). DEPLOY: NO.
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO.

================================================================================
*** PHASE R3-REV — REGISTRY WIRED INTO scan_pair_tf VIA _run_pattern_engine's
FIT + REASON STRINGS + LABELLER TOKENS (SHADOW-ONLY) — 2026-07-14 —
RESTART: YES (dexter.py + labeller.py edited), DEPLOY: NO,
RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
================================================================================

CONTEXT: this phase SUPERSEDES the original Phase R3, which was written
against the wrong engine. Investigation before any edits (no code changed in
that pass) established that patterns.py's run() -- the module Phases R1/R2
were built around -- is called only from api_analysis_engine() (a Flask
route; webapp display only, confirmed via a repo-wide grep of every
"patterns." reference in dexter.py). The autonomous scan loop that actually
reaches Chev, scan_pair_tf() (~9168, called concurrently per (symbol,
timeframe) pair via a ThreadPoolExecutor at ~13149), calls a wholly separate,
dexter-native engine instead: _run_pattern_engine() (~8396), with its own
inline fit_tl() trendline fit (last-up-to-5-pivots OLS), already feeding real
scoring (SCAN_WEIGHTS["pattern_breakout"] etc.) and real reason strings. Kev
ratified: the registry should track THIS engine's fit, since trust only
matters if it influences the decisions Chev actually sees. patterns.py stays
untouched and display-only; the visible PAT overlay and the line Chev is told
about are accepted as two closely-related but not identical lines (3-pivot vs
up-to-5-pivot fit) -- a known v1 caveat, not a bug, unification explicitly
deferred.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. ray_registry.py -- added REGISTRY_LOCK (threading.Lock) and updated the
   module docstring to describe the R3 wiring target. scan_pair_tf runs
   concurrently across pairs; a lock only around save_registry()'s own write
   would not have been enough, since the race is the WHOLE load-mutate-save
   span (two threads could each load the same on-disk state, mutate their own
   copies, and the second save silently discards the first's changes -- the
   same class of bug already fixed once for chev_journal.json/
   weight_overrides.json elsewhere in this project). Callers must hold
   REGISTRY_LOCK across their entire load -> reconcile -> update_touches ->
   update_break_state -> save sequence. Self-test extended with check 11:
   8 threads, each doing its OWN independent load->mutate->save round trip
   against the same file under the lock -- proves no symbol's ray is lost.
   22/22 (was 21/21).

2. dexter.py, _run_pattern_engine() (~8396) -- two ADDITIVE changes only,
   fit math (fit_tl, pivot detection, pattern scoring) untouched:
     a. geometry dict gained two new keys: upper_slope_raw / lower_slope_raw
        (the raw per-bar slope). upper_slope_norm/lower_slope_norm already
        there are price-normalized (per-mille of price), not the ATR-per-bar
        convention ray_registry.py needs, and neither is the raw slope needed
        to project the line forward/backward in time -- so it wasn't
        recoverable from the existing keys without adding these two.
     b. If no named pattern qualifies (results stays [] after every triangle/
        wedge/channel/rectangle/flag/pennant/H&S/double/triple check), the
        already-computed geometry vector was previously discarded entirely --
        the ray registry needs it every scan, independent of whether a named
        pattern forms (this was the whole point raised at the very start of
        this project's ray-line discussion: a bare respected diagonal with no
        named pattern is exactly the case that matters). Now appends one
        sentinel entry ({"name": "None", "confidence": 0.0, "breakout": False,
        "volume_confirmed": False, "category": "none", "details": {},
        "geometry": geometry}) mirroring patterns.py's own "pattern": "None"
        empty-result convention. VERIFIED SAFE by grepping every reader of
        _run_pattern_engine's return value in dexter.py: all_patterns's only
        emptiness-gate is `if all_patterns:` (~9411); pattern_result itself
        (the "pattern" key in scan_pair_tf's returned dict) is read NOWHERE
        else in the file (zero hits for result["pattern"]/result.get("pattern")
        anywhere); every reader of all_patterns downstream in ask_chev_to_judge
        (~10292-10230 area: _meaningful_pats filter, the breakout-level scan,
        the neckline-invalidation scan) gates on breakout/volume_confirmed/
        confidence>=0.55 or reads details/breakout_level -- all False/0.0/
        empty on the sentinel, so it is inert everywhere it could be read.

3. dexter.py, scan_pair_tf() -- the actual wiring, inserted after the Volume
   Profile block and before "Distance from level":
     - `import ray_registry` added alongside the existing engine imports.
     - Static levels captured for the future-crossing check WITHOUT
       recomputing anything: top_r/top_s (already-computed validated SR
       zones), fib_levels (already-computed dict), and VP POC/VAH/VAL --
       these last three needed one additive capture line inside the EXISTING
       VP loop (_ray_static_levels.append(...), unconditional, NOT gated on
       the existing proximity threshold, since a future-crossing candidate is
       by definition not at the level yet) -- the VP scoring logic itself
       untouched.
     - For each side (upper/lower): ATR from primary_df (skip entirely if
       unavailable), slope_norm = slope_raw/ATR, value-at-current-bar from
       geometry's upper_line/lower_line (already the projected value at the
       last bar -- confirmed by reading _run_pattern_engine's own upper_now/
       lower_now derivation). ray_registry.reconcile() -> update_touches() ->
       update_break_state(), all under REGISTRY_LOCK, then save_registry(),
       then select_live() (still under the lock, so it reads this thread's
       own just-saved state consistently rather than racing a concurrent
       thread's later write).
     - "Bars since last scan": a freshly minted ray gets just the current bar
       (not a speculative multi-bar lookback -- the fit itself only spans its
       last 3-5 pivots, crediting it with more history than that would
       overstate what's proven). A continuing ray processes only bars
       STRICTLY newer than its own last_seen_ts; if nothing has closed since
       (still the same forming candle, scanned again before it closed),
       touch/break processing is skipped entirely that round. SECOND-PASS
       FINDING, fixed before this was reported (see below): the first draft
       fell back to reprocessing the current bar whenever no new bar existed,
       which could double-count a touch against an earlier snapshot of the
       same still-forming candle -- corrected to skip instead.
     - Reason strings, at most one "Ray respected" and one "Ray confluence
       ahead" per selected live ray (ray_registry.select_live already caps at
       2 rays per side per symbol/timeframe): "Ray respected — {rising/
       falling/flat} {support/resistance}, held Nx over M.Mh, {bullish/
       bearish} (Xpt)" when price is currently within TOUCH_TOL_ATR x ATR of
       the ray; "Ray confluence ahead — approaching {level label} in ~N bars,
       {bullish/bearish}, tentative (Xpt)" when ray_registry.time_to_cross()
       finds a static-level crossing within the ray's horizon. Points via
       SCAN_WEIGHTS.get("ray_respected"/"ray_cross_ahead", 0.0) -- absent
       from SCAN_WEIGHTS/WEIGHT_LAB_VERIFIED_TAGS (grep-proof below), so both
       score 0.0 live today; hot-reloadable with zero code change once
       ratified, same as every other SCAN_WEIGHTS-backed tag. ray_reasons
       folded into all_reasons, ray_score folded into total_score, in the
       same expressions as every other confluence source.
     - The whole block wrapped in try/except mirroring api_analysis_engine's
       existing "[patterns.run] FAILED:" handling style exactly (bare
       `except Exception:`, traceback.print_exc(), never re-raised) --
       ray_reasons/ray_score reset to []/0.0 on any failure so a broken
       registry read/write can never break a scan or contaminate Chev's
       brief with partial data.

4. labeller.py -- two new REASON_MAP_ORDERED entries, placed FIRST (before
   even the "[WATCH..." entries), with a comment explaining why: ray reason
   strings are full sentences that deliberately reuse other reason types'
   vocabulary inside them (e.g. "...approaching Fib 61.8%...", "...rising
   support..."), so if any Fib/SR/GP/etc. entry were checked first in the
   substring-match, first-match-wins loop, it would steal the token before
   the ray-specific entry ever got a chance. Verified against the FULL
   ordered table (not assumed): no existing entry's pattern is a substring of
   "Ray respected"/"Ray confluence ahead" themselves, so placing these two
   first costs nothing and fixes everything downstream. Also verified the
   step-1 S/R regex (_SR_RE, anchored `^(Resistance|Support)\(`) cannot fire
   on either string (they don't start with those literals), and the step-2
   pattern regex (_PATTERN_RE, literal "conf=") cannot fire either -- "conf="
   does not appear even though "confluence" contains the substring "conf".
   Self-test extended (32/32, was 26/26) with 6 new checks (14e-14h): a
   string containing "support" maps ONLY to ray_respected, no sr_single/
   sr_multi leak; same for "resistance"; the exact "Ray confluence ahead ...
   Fib 61.8% ..." collision case proves ray_cross_ahead wins over fib_618
   (first-match-wins, not just asserted); both ray_respected examples
   confirmed to literally carry the word "bullish"/"bearish" as required;
   confirmed neither ray string ever triggers _PATTERN_RE's pattern tokens.

TASK 4 -- shadow-only confirmed end to end. Grep-proof (programmatic, not
eyeballed): neither "ray_respected" nor "ray_cross_ahead" appears in the
SCAN_WEIGHTS or WEIGHT_LAB_VERIFIED_TAGS dict literal bodies. Read
weight_proposal.py's build_design_matrix() (~240): tag_counts is built by
iterating `for t in r["features"]` across every shadow record dynamically --
there is no fixed tag enumeration anywhere in that file. Any tag appearing in
labels_closed.jsonl's "features" list is automatically counted, and once it
reaches MIN_N=30 occurrences it's included in the regression and reported on
-- confirmed, not assumed. So ray_respected/ray_cross_ahead will surface in
future weight_proposal.py runs automatically, with zero code change to that
file, once enough shadow samples exist; no STOP was needed.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,

select_live() is called against the WHOLE registry (flattened across every

scan's own symbol/timeframe -- correct, but a mild and growing inefficiency
as the watchlist/registry grows, since select_live's internal grouping work
is repeated for every scan even for symbols irrelevant to it. Worth a future
optimization (pre-filter before calling select_live) if the watchlist grows
large enough for this to matter; not fixed now per "smallest possible diff."

*** PHASE R4 — WHAT CHEV SEES (FACT FRAMING, BUDGETED) — 2026-07-14 —
RESTART: YES, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
================================================================================

CONTEXT: the ray registry (R2) and its wiring into the real scan loop (R3)
give Dexter persistent ray identity and trust, but Chev never saw any of it
-- this phase surfaces it, as plain stated fact, in the two places Chev
reads: the escalation message (ask_chev_to_judge) and the 30-minute
checkpoint (ask_chev_manage_trade). No ray tool exists for Chev to call, so
the checkpoint gets an inline DATA block, not a tool instruction. A hard
token budget already governs the escalation message (≤14k combined, ≤8k
brief, proven by the standalone audit_context.py) -- this phase had to prove
the new block fits inside it, not just claim it does.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. ray_registry.py -- format_ray_block_for_chev(rays, current_price,
   timeframe, levels=None), mirroring engines.py's format_invalidation_
   candidates_for_chev / format_validation_candidates_for_chev style: takes
   an already select_live()-filtered, single-(symbol,timeframe) list (this
   function recomputes nothing), returns "" when empty -- not a "none
   found" line, since a bare respected ray is common enough that a line on
   every escalation would be noise (invalidation always shows something
   because the skip discipline requires it; a ray doesn't). Per ray: slope
   class + side, value now, value at horizon (in the timeframe's own bar
   count with a wall-clock hour estimate), lifetime record (respected Nx,
   M wick-traps, over Hh), and the nearest crossing if a `levels` list was
   given. One additional channel line when both an upper and lower ray are
   present with slope_norms within SLOPE_MATCH_TOL of each other -- both
   boundary values now and at horizon, plus price's position within the
   channel as a percentage, descriptive only. FACT FRAMING ONLY, verified by
   a self-test check (12f) that greps the rendered block for a banned-word
   list (must/confirm before/wait for/favours/bullish/bearish) and asserts
   none appear -- not just asserted in a comment. CAUGHT BEFORE SHIPPING: the
   function originally took an `atr` parameter that nothing in its body
   actually used (every value it renders is already ATR-normalized on the
   RayRecord at reconcile() time) -- removed rather than left as dead
   weight, which simplified both call sites (no ATR fetch needed at all in
   the checkpoint caller).

2. dexter.py, ask_chev_to_judge() -- ray_block computed after validation_
   block, injected via f"{ray_block}" immediately after f"{validation_
   block}". Read the _near_sup/_near_res long/short/both selection logic
   first (invalidation/validation build "(IF LONG)"/"(IF SHORT)" duplicate
   variants because those candidates are PRICED FROM ENTRY, which differs
   by direction when Chev hasn't committed to one yet) -- concluded, and
   state here explicitly, that the ray block does NOT need that
   duplication: ray facts (value/horizon/record) aren't priced from entry
   and don't depend on which direction Chev eventually picks, so a single
   block covering both sides is correct, not a shortcut. The static levels
   for the crossing check reuse result["support"]/["resistance"]/["fibs"]
   (already computed by scan_pair_tf for this exact symbol/timeframe, not
   recomputed). Registry access is read-only (no lock -- save_registry's
   atomic os.replace means a concurrent writer can never produce a torn
   read); wrapped in try/except mirroring the existing failure-handling
   style, never raises, falls back to "".

3. dexter.py, ask_chev_manage_trade() -- ray_checkpoint_block computed once
   (shared by both the SIP-active and normal branches) right after
   tool_instructions is built, spliced into BOTH message variants via
   f"{ray_checkpoint_block}" immediately after f"{tool_instructions}".
   Explicitly labelled "DATA Dexter already fetched (no tool call needed for
   this):" when non-empty -- never phrased as an instruction to call
   anything, per the phase's explicit rule (no ray tool exists for Chev).
   No `levels` passed (ask_chev_manage_trade doesn't have Fib/SR/VP in scope
   the way scan_pair_tf does, and recomputing them for a periodic checkpoint
   isn't worth it) -- format_ray_block_for_chev's optional argument already
   handles that cleanly (ray facts still shown, no crossing line). ATR for
   select_live()'s distinctness threshold comes from trade["atr_at_entry"]
   (a real snapshot already stored at entry time, confirmed by grep -- NOT
   an invented proxy; an earlier draft used abs(entry-original_SL) as a
   stand-in for ATR before this was caught and replaced during
   implementation, since risk distance is not ATR and that would have been
   a genuinely unjustified approximation).

4. audit_context.py -- extended per Task 4:
     a. Added a worst-case ray_block sample (2 live rays, opposite sides,
        slopes within SLOPE_MATCH_TOL so the channel line renders, 2
        crossings -- levels deliberately chosen to sit within EACH ray's
        own horizon so both crossing lines actually render, not an
        accidental best case) using the real format_ray_block_for_chev,
        imported from ray_registry.py (safe: that module has zero dexter
        import, zero import-time side effects, confirmed by re-reading it).
        Spliced into the escalation msg reproduction at the same relative
        position as dexter.py's real change, and added to the existing
        per-section token inventory.
     b. Added a NEW "PHASE R4 -- CHECKPOINT COPY" section -- this did not
        exist before this phase; the checkpoint message had never been
        measured here at all. Reproduces tool_instructions verbatim plus
        the checkpoint's ray block (same synthetic rays, no levels, wrapped
        in the same "DATA Dexter already fetched" label dexter.py now
        prepends) and prints its own token total. Stated explicitly: the
        14k/8k gates are defined for the ESCALATION message specifically --
        there is no separately-defined budget for the checkpoint message,
        so this section makes its real cost visible without inventing a
        gate nobody set.

BENEFIT: Chev can now read, as plain stated fact with no framing pressure,
where a trusted diagonal line sits, where it's projected to be by the time a
typical trade plays out, how many times it's actually proven itself, and
whether its path is heading toward another known level -- exactly the
"predict the future" capability this whole build exists for -- without a
single word of it being coded as a suggestion, a requirement, or a directive
Chev is expected to obey.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,
re-reading the diff cold): traced every module touched directly (ray_

checkpoint's try/except blocks both fall back to "" on any failure, matching
the existing failure-handling style exactly; confirmed result["support"]/

actually returns, not assumed from the key name. One pre-existing pattern
reused as-is, not re-litigated: select_live() is still called against the

documented, growing-but-not-yet-material inefficiency flagged in the R3
handoff) -- not fixed here, out of scope for a "what Chev sees" phase.

VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile dexter.py labeller.py ray_registry.py
audit_context.py` -> exit 0 on all four. `python -X utf8 derivs.py` ->
12/12 PASS (unchanged). `python labeller.py` -> 32/32 PASS (unchanged --
this phase never touches labeller.py). `python -X utf8 ray_registry.py` ->

================================================================================
*** PHASE R5 — RAY BREAK = URGENT ALERT (PER-RAY ONE-SHOT) — 2026-07-14 —
RESTART: YES, DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***
================================================================================

CONTEXT: R4 put ray status into the routine 30-minute checkpoint, but a ray
breaking WHILE a trade is open — the moment Chev's stated thesis may actually
be dying — had no path to reach him faster than the next scheduled check.
_maybe_send_bos_alert already does exactly this for market-structure breaks:
detects a new BOS/CHoCH, fires an urgent ask_chev_manage_trade call bypassing
the 30-minute cooldown via a background thread. A confirmed ray break (Phase
R2's two-close rule) is the same category of event.

TASK 1 (read before writing, reported here): _maybe_send_bos_alert (dexter.py
~10837) is called once per open trade, every check_and_update_open_trades
loop iteration (that loop itself runs every scan cycle for crypto, on its own
gated interval for forex/stock). It fetches candles fresh EVERY call
(fetch_candles, a live network hit), recomputes _bos_choch_label(df) fresh
every time, and dedups via a fingerprint set living directly on the trade
dict (trade["bos_alerts_sent"], lazily initialized, never explicitly
persisted anywhere outside the in-memory trade dict — the same fragility
BOS itself already accepts). It bypasses ask_chev_manage_trade's 30-minute
cooldown by passing a non-None bos_paragraph — that function's cooldown
check is literally `if bos_paragraph is None and (...): return None`, so ANY
non-None paragraph, from ANY caller, skips the wait entirely by design. The
actual LLM call happens in a daemon background thread
(threading.Thread(target=lambda ...: ask_chev_manage_trade(...), daemon=
True).start()) so the main loop never blocks on it.
ALSO FOUND, NOT TOUCHED: bos_paragraph's construction has a real operator-
precedence bug — three adjacent f-string literals concatenate into ONE atom
before the trailing `if bos.get("hold") else ""` ternary ever binds, so
depending on truthiness of "hold" either the opening lines (urgency/what-
happened) or the closing lines (watch-for + explanatory text) silently
vanish from the message, never both together. In practice this never fires:
_bos_choch_label's only case with hold=None ("STRUCTURE UNCLEAR") is already
filtered out by _maybe_send_bos_alert's own early return before the
paragraph is ever built. Left untouched per this build's rule that the BOS
function stay byte-identical (grep-diff proved below) and per general
instructions not to fix unrelated pre-existing bugs; format_ray_break_
paragraph_for_chev (new, this phase) deliberately does NOT reproduce this
construction.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. ray_registry.py — two new PURE functions, no I/O, added for a reason
   beyond style: dexter.py has no `if __name__ == "__main__"` guard anywhere
   (confirmed by grep — its main scan loop, `while True:` ~13399, sits at
   true module level), so `import dexter` would start the live bot
   immediately. The only way to satisfy this phase's GATE requirement for an
   offline, no-bot-run test of the fire/skip/paragraph logic was to make
   that logic live somewhere importable without side effects.
     - select_break_alert_candidate(rays, already_alerted_ids): returns the
       first BROKEN ray (any side) whose id is not in the caller's
       already-alerted set, or None. Does not read/write RayRecord.
       alerted_trade_ids itself — that field is a separate, caller-managed
       persisted record.
     - format_ray_break_paragraph_for_chev(ray, symbol, timeframe,
       still_valid_line): builds the exact "what happened / still valid if /
       watch for" shape BOS uses, correctly (no adjacent-literal-plus-
       ternary bug), fact-framed. Takes a plain string for still_valid_line
       so the formatter itself stays trade-dict-agnostic.

2. dexter.py — _maybe_send_ray_break_alert(trade, current_price), placed
   directly after _maybe_send_bos_alert, invoked immediately after it at the
   SAME call site inside check_and_update_open_trades' per-trade loop (same
   cadence, same guards, same try/except-never-raises safety net). Reads the
   registry (no fetch, no recompute — the whole point is reusing what
   scan_pair_tf's R3 wiring already computed), finds a not-yet-alerted
   BROKEN ray for this trade's symbol+timeframe via the pure selector above,
   marks it alerted in trade["ray_alerts_sent"] (a set, mirroring
   trade["bos_alerts_sent"] exactly — same fragility accepted, per Task 2's
   explicit instruction to follow how BOS persists its own per-trade flag),
   ALSO appends the trade's row-id to the ray's own alerted_trade_ids (the
   RayRecord field reserved for this exact purpose since Phase R2 — a
   secondary, persisted record that survives a restart even though the
   trade-side set doesn't; NOT consulted for the fire/skip decision, which
   is the trade-side set only). "Still valid if" pulls trade.get(
   "invalidation") or trade.get("reasoning") — confirmed by reading
   ask_chev_manage_trade's own context-building code that trade dicts really
   do carry these fields (not assumed), with an honest fallback sentence
   when neither is recorded rather than fabricating one. Fires via the same
   threading.Thread(daemon=True) pattern, reusing ask_chev_manage_trade's
   existing bos_paragraph= parameter as-is (its role is generically "urgent
   paragraph, bypass cooldown," not literally BOS-specific — reusing it
   avoids touching that function's signature at all).
   TASK 3 (double-fire guard): BOS and this new function are now BOTH
   urgent-bypass callers of the same trade's management cycle in the same
   loop iteration. ask_chev_manage_trade's cooldown check only protects
   ROUTINE (bos_paragraph=None) calls — any non-None paragraph, from EITHER
   caller, skips it entirely, so the shared cooldown gives no protection
   between two urgent callers. BOS itself has no guard against this (until
   this phase there was only one urgent-bypass source, so the collision
   couldn't happen). Per the phase's explicit instruction, the minimal guard
   was added to the NEW function ONLY: RAY_ALERT_DEDUP_WINDOW_SEC (10
   seconds, a "same breath" window, unrelated to and much shorter than the
   real 30-minute cooldown) — skip if ANY management call, routine or
   urgent, touched trade["last_management_at"] within the last 10 seconds.
   HONEST LIMITATION, stated plainly: this is best-effort, not a hard
   guarantee. BOS's own background thread updates last_management_at
   asynchronously (inside ask_chev_manage_trade, which is the thread's own
   target function) — if BOS decides to fire in the SAME iteration
   immediately before this function runs, there is a real window where that
   thread hasn't started yet and last_management_at is still stale, so this
   guard would not catch it. Closing that window completely would require
   touching either BOS or ask_chev_manage_trade's cooldown gate for every
   caller, both explicitly out of scope. Flagged here rather than silently
   presented as fully solved.

BENEFIT: a ray that was cited (or plausibly relevant) as part of a trade's
thesis, breaking while that trade is open, now reaches Chev within roughly
one loop iteration instead of waiting up to 30 minutes — with the specific
what-broke/still-valid-if/watch-for facts he needs to decide whether to
reconsider, exactly the "give Chev the opportunity to withdraw a trade"
capability this whole ray build set out to add, using the exact same urgent-
delivery mechanism already trusted for structure breaks rather than
inventing a new one.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,
re-reading the diff cold): traced every module touched directly (ray_
registry.py's two new pure functions, dexter.py's new function + one new
invocation line) and indirectly (ask_chev_manage_trade — confirmed its
bos_paragraph handling is generic and unaffected by a second caller; BOS
itself — confirmed untouched by grep-diff, twice). ONE REAL BUG FOUND AND
FIXED before this was reported: the first draft called
ray_registry.load_registry() OUTSIDE REGISTRY_LOCK and only acquired the
lock around the final save_registry() call — this re-opens the exact lost-
update race the lock exists to prevent (a concurrent scan_pair_tf write
landing in the gap between this function's unlocked read and its locked
write would be silently overwritten by this function's now-stale snapshot
on save). Fixed by moving the lock acquisition to wrap the entire load ->
select -> mutate -> save sequence, matching ray_registry.py's own documented
contract exactly. Re-verified all tests pass after the fix. Also caught
during the same pass, fixed as a small consistency item: select_break_alert_
candidate's already_alerted_ids parameter had no type hint, inconsistent
with every other typed function in the module — added (Set[str], with Set
added to the typing import).

audit_context.py test_ray_break_alert.py test_ray_extension.py` -> exit 0 on

labeller.py` -> 32/32 PASS (unchanged — this phase never touches
