TASK 1 (read before writing): api_analysis_engine() (dexter.py ~2459) is a
plain, unauthenticated GET route (no @require_key — read-only analysis
routes in this webapp don't carry it), symbol/tf from flask_request.args,
try/except returning jsonify({"error": str(e)}), 500. Modeled the new route
on this exactly. select_live()'s extended signature (Phase R3) needs
current_bar_ts and atr_by_key. Neither is fetched live in the new route
(read-only, no recompute, per the hard rules): current_bar_ts is wall-clock
time.time(), the same choice already made for the read-only Chev-facing
paths in Phase R4. atr_by_key is RECOVERED from the registry records
themselves — slope_norm is already ATR-per-bar (baked in by the scan side at
reconcile() time), so |slope_raw / slope_norm| recovers the ATR in effect
when a ray was last reconciled; median across whatever rays already exist
for the requested (symbol, tf) key. Confirmed by reading select_live()
itself that it already excludes any ray whose state != "LIVE" before doing
anything else — so BROKEN rays are excluded automatically, no extra
filtering needed in the route.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. dexter.py — GET /api/rays?symbol=...&tf=..., placed directly after
   api_analysis_engine(). Loads the registry read-only under REGISTRY_LOCK
   (an explicit instruction for this phase; note the lock is scoped to JUST
   the load_registry() call, correctly, since this route does zero writes —
   unlike Phase R5's read-modify-write case, there's no stale-snapshot race
   to guard against here). Calls select_live() (unmodified) and, per ray,
   ray_registry's own _project_value/horizon_bars/_TF_SECONDS (unmodified;
   no new projection math written) to compute four coordinate pairs:
   t_anchor/p_anchor (the ray's own anchor, no projection needed),
   t_now/p_now (value at current_bar_ts), t_horizon/p_horizon (value at
   horizon_bars(ray) bars ahead, timestamp extrapolated by the timeframe's

   established in Phase R4's format_ray_block_for_chev, reused a second
   time, not reinvented). slope_class (rising/falling/flat) uses the exact
   same sign-based classification as Phases R4/R5's Chev-facing text, so the

   words anything. Staleness: "one scan cycle" reuses dexter.py's own

   cadence) — if last_seen_ts is older than that, the label gets a

   -> {"rays": []}, HTTP 200 (plain jsonify, no error). Sanity-verified

   see Phase R5's handoff for why; same constraint applies here) with a

*** PHASE R6 — BOUNDARY PURITY GATE (ADAPTED FROM PARTNER'S chat.js
VALIDATION) — 2026-07-14 — RESTART: YES (dexter.py touched at the wiring
point), DEPLOY: NO, RE-PASTE CHEV PROMPT: NO ***

CONTEXT: the client-side TL tool (chat.js, _computeTrendlines) already has
two validation ideas the ray registry lacked: a PIERCE TEST (reject a line
price closed beyond) and a TRENDING FILTER (reject near-flat lines -- those
belong to horizontal S/R). This phase ports both into ray_registry.py as a
NARRATION gate, not a tracking gate: a gated ray keeps its identity, touch
tallies, and break state exactly as before, and (critically) still fires
Phase R5's break alert -- it is only excluded from reason emission, from
format_ray_block_for_chev, and demoted (not excluded) in select_live.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. ray_registry.py -- three new constants: PIERCE_TOL_ATR=0.6 (matches
   chat.js's own default tolerance, `opts.tolAtr || 0.6`, chat.js ~587);
   PIERCE_MAX=0 (any confirmed pierce disqualifies narration -- a constant
   specifically so loosening it later is a deliberate, visible edit, not
   drift); TRENDING_MIN_SLOPE_NORM=0.15 (identical bar to _run_pattern_
   engine's flat_thr = atr * 0.15, dexter.py ~8514 -- slope_norm is already
   ATR-per-bar, the same units that threshold uses, cited so the two never
   drift apart silently). New RayRecord field pierce_count (int, default 0
   -- a pre-R6 JSON record missing this key loads as 0 via the dataclass
   default, no special-case load_registry() code needed; proved with a test
   against a hand-built pre-R6-shaped JSON record, not just assumed).
   New count_boundary_pierces(bars, ray_value_at, side, atr): pure, counts
   bars whose CLOSE lands beyond the line by more than PIERCE_TOL_ATR x ATR
   on the wrong side. Deliberately diverges from chat.js, which tests highs/
   lows (wicks): a wick beyond the line is already trap evidence FOR the
   line via update_touches' wick_rejection_count -- counting the same wick
   again here as a strike against the line would directly contradict that.
   Takes a projection CALLABLE rather than a RayRecord (matching the design
   spec's exact signature) so it has nothing to mutate; the caller
   accumulates ray.pierce_count += count_boundary_pierces(...) itself.
   New is_narratable(ray): pierce_count <= PIERCE_MAX AND |slope_norm| >=
   TRENDING_MIN_SLOPE_NORM AND state == "LIVE".
   PLACEMENT DECISION (read update_touches first, as instructed): pierce-
   counting is a PARALLEL pure step, not merged into update_touches's
   internals. Reason: update_touches already mutates the ray directly (a
   touch-open/close state machine); count_boundary_pierces is pure by design
   (no ray reference at all) and simply returns a count for the SAME
   incremental "bars since last scan" slice update_touches/update_break_
   state already receive -- this is the exact same "walk the same small bar
   list via independent functions, once each" pattern already established
   in this module (update_touches and update_break_state already do this;
   this is a third parallel walk, not a new idea). Does NOT re-walk the
   ray's whole lifetime -- it only ever sees the same incremental bars the
   other two functions see, accumulating incrementally scan over scan.
   format_ray_block_for_chev now filters its input to is_narratable rays
   before rendering anything (a safety net, not trusting the caller already
   filtered -- select_live only demotes, doesn't exclude, so a gated ray can
   still arrive here). select_live's sort key gained is_narratable as the
   PRIMARY key (narratable sorts as True > False), existing respect_count/
   r-squared ordering preserved as secondary/tertiary keys within each
   narratable-or-not group -- a gated ray can still fill a remaining slot if
   there's no narratable candidate, demoted, never excluded. reconcile()'s
   MATCHED/MINTED log lines and _retire_stale()'s RETIRED log line each
   gained pierce_count and narratable fields for observability.

2. dexter.py -- three call sites, exactly as scoped, nothing else touched:
     a. R3's per-scan ray wiring: right after update_touches/update_break_
        state (same _ray_bars slice, same place), _ray_obj.pierce_count +=
        ray_registry.count_boundary_pierces(...) using a
        `lambda ts: ray_registry._project_value(_ray_obj, ts)` projection.
     b. The "Ray respected"/"Ray confluence ahead" reason-emission loop:
        one `if not ray_registry.is_narratable(_ray_obj): continue` added
        at the top of the per-ray loop body -- skips reason emission only;
        identity/touches/break-state/alerts for this same ray are computed
        earlier in the SAME wiring block and are entirely unaffected.
     c. /api/rays (Phase W1): one additional filter line after the existing
        symbol/tf filter, since select_live() only demotes -- W1 HAS landed
        (confirmed by reading it), and it was returning every selected ray
        with no narratable filter, meaning it WOULD now show a gated ray on
        the chart as if it were narrated. Fixed for consistency: the chart
        must not show a ray Chev never received a reason about.
   VERIFIED, NOT ASSUMED: R5's select_break_alert_candidate() does not call
   is_narratable anywhere (read its full body -- it gates only on state ==
   "BROKEN" and the caller's own already-alerted set) -- confirmed both by
   reading the source AND empirically: test_ray_break_alert.py's existing
   15 checks all still pass unmodified, using a broken_ray fixture whose
   slope_norm (0.04) is flat/non-narratable, and it is still correctly
   selected for alerting. A flat or pierced ray breaking during an open
   trade is still tradeable information and still alerts.
   Also verified: ask_chev_manage_trade's checkpoint call to format_ray_
   block_for_chev (Phase R4) needed ZERO changes -- the gate lives inside
   the shared formatter itself, so both of dexter.py's two call sites (the
   escalation path and the checkpoint path) inherit it automatically.

3. audit_context.py -- its worst-case ray-block sample (shared by both the
   escalation and checkpoint sections) used the exact same synthetic slope
   values (-0.05/0.04) that Phase R4's own ray_registry.py self-test used --
   both were now sub-threshold under the new TRENDING_MIN_SLOPE_NORM=0.15
   gate, which would have made format_ray_block_for_chev silently render ""
   for what was supposed to demonstrate the WORST case. Bumped both files'
   fixture slopes to -0.2/-0.15 (still within SLOPE_MATCH_TOL of each other
   so the channel line still renders too) and recomputed the crossing
   levels so both still land within each ray's horizon. Re-ran the audit:
   token counts are essentially unchanged (113/105, same as before this
   phase) and the COMBINED TOTAL is byte-for-byte the same verdict (10,197
   tokens, under the 14k gate by 3,803) -- confirming the phase's own
   expectation that "the block format didn't change, only which rays
   qualify" held true once the fixtures were corrected to describe a
   genuinely narratable ray again.

BENEFIT: Chev (and now the webapp chart, via W1) only ever hears about or
sees a diagonal line that has actually behaved like a real boundary -- one
price has closed beyond never counts against a trap, but a real close
through disqualifies the line from being narrated as clean, and a merely
flat line never gets mistaken for a trending one. Nothing about the
underlying fit, tracking, or alerting changed -- only which rays earn the
right to be TALKED ABOUT.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,
re-reading the diff cold): traced every function touched directly (the two
new pure functions, the three call sites, the two log-line/self-test
extensions) and indirectly (R5's alert path -- confirmed independent both
by reading and by its unmodified tests still passing; the R4 checkpoint
call site -- confirmed it needed no change; _run_pattern_engine and chat.js
-- confirmed byte-identical, see VERIFICATION). One thing considered and
deliberately NOT changed: count_boundary_pierces has no access to ray.state
(its signature takes a projection callable, not a RayRecord, per the
phase's exact spec), so dexter.py's wiring calls it unconditionally even
for a ray that update_break_state may have JUST flipped to BROKEN earlier
in the same bar list -- meaning pierce_count keeps accumulating on an
already-broken ray. Traced whether this has any observable effect: none --
is_narratable's state == "LIVE" check already excludes a BROKEN ray from
narration regardless of its pierce_count, so this is inert bookkeeping, not
a bug. Left as-is rather than adding a guard for a code path with zero
behavioral consequence. One test-authoring bug caught and fixed during
self-test construction itself (not a bug in shipped ray_registry.py logic):
the first draft of the wick-through-vs-pierce interaction test (13b) used a
trending (non-zero slope) ray, so the line's projected value drifted upward
between the two test bars -- the second bar's hand-picked "close on the
correct side" value was only correct for a flat line, causing a false test
failure. Fixed by making that specific fixture flat (slope_raw=0), since
13b tests the touch/pierce interaction, not narratability.

VERIFICATION: `python -m py_compile dexter.py labeller.py ray_registry.py
audit_context.py` -> exit 0 on all four. `python -X utf8 derivs.py` ->
12/12 PASS (unchanged). `python labeller.py` -> 32/32 PASS (unchanged --
this phase never touches labeller.py). `python -X utf8 ray_registry.py` ->
41/41 PASS (28 existing + 13 new: mid-span close-through counts as exactly
one pierce and disqualifies narration; wick-through-and-reject registers
zero pierces while wick_rejection_count still increments via the SAME bars,
proving the two walks don't double-count or interfere; a flat ray still
accumulates a respected touch but stays non-narratable; a close exactly AT
the pierce tolerance boundary is not a pierce, just beyond it is; slope_norm
exactly AT the trending threshold IS narratable, just below is not; a

PHASE W2 -- NAMES AND BIAS ON THE PAT OVERLAY

CONTEXT: The webapp's PAT overlay (patterns.py, api_analysis_engine, the
"Pattern trendlines" section of engine.js's _drawEngineOverlays) was drawing
the two boundary lines of a detected pattern with no name or read on-chart --
Kev had to already know what a "descending triangle" looks like and reason
out its bias himself. This phase adds a short name + confidence + one plain-
English bias sentence directly on the chart, computed server-side from data
Dexter already has (patterns.py's own category/bias fields, plus engines.py's
existing state.direction), with zero new pattern-detection or market math and
zero changes to patterns.py itself.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. dexter.py -- two new small pure functions placed immediately before
   @flask_app.route("/api/analysis/engine") (line ~2468):
     a. _pat_prior_trend_bucket(direction) -- buckets state_out["direction"]
        into "up"/"down"/"range" using the SAME +25/-25 threshold engine.js's
        own mood-emoji logic already uses, for consistency with an existing
        convention rather than inventing a new one.
     b. _pat_bias_text(category, pattern_bias, prior_trend) -- maps pattern.
        category ("continuation"/"reversal"/"neutral") x pattern.bias
        ("bullish"/"bearish"/"neutral") x prior_trend to one descriptive (never
        directive -- no "buy"/"long"/"short") sentence. Verified against
        Kev's own worked example: a descending triangle in an uptrend reads
        as "against the prior trend -- consolidation, not a clean
        continuation"; the same triangle in a downtrend reads as "aligned --
        continuing it."
   Inside api_analysis_engine(), right after the existing patterns.run()
   try/except block and before the route's return jsonify(...): when
   patterns_out has a real named pattern, patterns_out["display"] = {name,
   confidence_pct (rounded from the existing value*100), bias_text} is added;
   otherwise patterns_out["display"] = None. Every existing key (pattern,
   bias, category, value, upper_trendline, lower_trendline) is read, never
   altered -- patterns.py itself was not opened for editing.

2. webapp/js/charts/engine.js -- inside _drawEngineOverlays()'s existing
   section 4 ("Pattern trendlines"), immediately after the two established
   _drawPatternLine() calls: when pat.display is non-null, compute the
   pattern's horizontal midpoint and draw two _lbl() calls (name + confidence
   above, bias sentence below) at that point -- reusing the same on-chart
   text primitive S/R, VP, and RSI-projection labels already use, not a new
   labeling system. Both strings are printed verbatim from the API; nothing
   is worded in JS.
   SECOND-PASS FINDING, FIXED BEFORE SHIPPING: the first draft computed the
   midpoint as (uEp.t1 + uEp.t2) / 2 directly. But Phase R1 (this same
   build's earlier fix) made patterns.py's boundary lines extend ~25 bars
   PAST the last real candle so the ray keeps drawing forward -- meaning
   uEp.t2 is now genuinely a future timestamp, and using it unmodified would
   drag the label away from the pattern's actual historical shape and toward
   that future extrapolation. Found the exact same problem already solved
   elsewhere in this codebase (drawing.js:2850/2910, the VP drawing tool):
   capping the far endpoint at currentCandles' last real timestamp via
   Math.min(). Applied the identical idiom here rather than inventing a new
   one -- the label now sits within the pattern's visible historical body.

3. webapp/index.html -- engine.js's ?v= bumped to 20260722-2 (single bump
   covers both this phase's engine.js edits).

Nothing else touched. patterns.py, _run_pattern_engine, ray_registry.py,
chat.js, and every prior phase's code are untouched (confirmed below).

BENEFIT: Kev sees the pattern's name, Dexter's confidence in it, and a plain-
English read of whether it's likely to continue or reverse given the actual
prior trend -- directly on the chart, without having to recall pattern theory
himself or cross-reference the state engine's direction number by hand.
No new detection logic, no directive language, no change to what Chev
receives (this phase is chart-only, matching the build's global scope).

PHASE W3 -- "WHAT CHEV SEES": SCAN-ENGINE PATTERN VIEW

CONTEXT: _run_pattern_engine (dexter.py) is the pattern engine that actually
feeds Chev via scan_pair_tf's real scan loop -- a richer, independent detector
(flags, pennants, channels, proper 5-point H&S, in addition to what
patterns.py's "PAT" overlay already draws) that had no chart presence at all.
Kev wanted to see, on the chart, exactly what THIS engine currently detects.
This phase adds a read-only endpoint plus a new "SCAN" chart overlay, entirely
separate from PAT, with zero changes to either engine's fit/detection math.

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. dexter.py -- _run_pattern_engine's `geometry` dict (shared across every
   pattern entry a single call returns) gained 5 additive keys, appended after
   the existing R3 keys, values only, nothing altered: window_len (n, the
   tail-windowed df's length), upper_ref_idx/lower_ref_idx (the first pivot's
   LOCAL bar index used by fit_tl -- exactly `ref_x = x[0]` already computed
   inside fit_tl, just not previously returned), upper_ref_price/
   lower_ref_price (that same fitted line's value at that index -- the
   regression intercept `b`, not necessarily the raw pivot price). Combined
   with the already-existing upper_line/lower_line (fitted value at the LAST
   window bar) and upper_slope_raw/lower_slope_raw (R3), these fully describe
   both boundary lines as two (t, p) endpoints without touching a single line
   of the fit math itself. Grep-confirmed (see VERIFICATION) the function's
   internals are otherwise byte-identical -- this is a pure append to one
   dict literal.

   New route: GET /api/scan_patterns?symbol=...&tf=... -- fetches candles the
   same way api_analysis_engine() does (same fetch_candles(sym, atype, tf,
   500) call, same clean/atype logic, not a new fetcher), calls
   engines.run_survey(...) for the prior-trend signal (same call already
   proven safe in api_analysis_engine, same argument shape) and
   _run_pattern_engine(df) unchanged, then for the top 3 patterns (already
   sorted best-first by the engine's own priority: breakout+volume >
   breakout > confidence) converts each one's shared geometry into two
   {t1,p1,t2,p2,slope_class,r2} endpoint objects using the additive fields
   above (outer_idx = len(df) - window_len + local_idx, timestamp via
   df.index[outer_idx].timestamp() -- the same bare convention already used
   for anchor_ts elsewhere in this exact ray-wiring family, e.g.
   primary_df.index[-1].timestamp() at the R3 site), and composes a Python-
   side display object (name, confidence_pct, bias_text) by calling W2's
   existing _pat_prior_trend_bucket/_pat_bias_text -- imported by reference,
   not duplicated. Entries with name=="None" (the R3 sentinel) or missing
   window_len (an older/partial geometry shape) are skipped, not erroneously
   drawn. Purely additive to the pattern engine's return shape; no registry,
   reason, or scoring code touched. Read-only, same try/except-to-{"error"}
   contract as every other route in this build.

2. webapp/js/charts/engine.js --
     a. _engineOverlayState gained `scanPatterns: false`; a new module state
        var `_scanPatternsData` (mirrors `_tlRaysData`'s shape: its own
        endpoint, its own cache-or-fetch-by-symbol+tf check, never touching
        `_engineData`).
     b. _drawEngineOverlays() gained section 6 ("Scan-engine patterns"),
        appended after section 5 (rays), before the function's closing
        dctx.restore(). Draws each pattern's two boundary lines dotted
        ([2,3] dash) in blue (#2962ff, the existing drawing-tool palette
        accent already used for the ctxColors swatch) -- visually distinct
        from section 4's PAT lines (dashed [6,4], red/green/gold) per the
        phase's explicit requirement. Label (name + confidence + " (scan)",
        then bias_text) reuses _lbl(), the same primitive W1/W2/S/R/VP/RSI
        labels already use. Deliberately does NOT apply W2's last-real-
        candle midpoint capping fix -- unlike patterns.py's R1-extended
        lines, this engine's t2 is always the outer df's actual last row
        (never future-projected), so the fix doesn't apply here; noted
        explicitly rather than copied blindly.
     c. New "SCAN" Arsenal tool, following drawPatternLines()/
        drawRegistryRays()'s exact three-function shape:

     d. ?v= bumped to 20260722-3 (this build's date-sequence convention).

3. webapp/index.html -- one new Layers-tab grid row, `lyrScanCard`
   ("SCAN"/"Chev's Patterns"), inserted immediately after `lyrPatCard`, using

   checkbox + `toolDot` + `ltbName` button + `ltbDesc`) -- NOT the
   `hasDropdown`/`.ltbDrop`/`ltbArrow` variant TL and Fib use. Chosen over a
   TL-style dropdown because PAT (the card SCAN sits beside) has no existing
   arrow/popup infrastructure to extend, and _ctpShow (chat.js)'s shared
   popup is hardcoded to four specific body ids (fib/rsi/tl/vp) with its own
   titles map -- retrofitting a fifth would touch a shared function and add
   new popup markup for a plain on/off toggle that doesn't need TF-style
   sub-options. A third, self-contained layer card mirrors an already-proven
   complete pattern (PAT itself) and is the smaller, more consistent diff.
   ?v= bump covered under item 2d (same file, same version stamp).

PHASE R7 -- TIMEFRAME TABLE FIX + GAP-WINDOW HARDENING IN ray_registry.py

CONTEXT: ray_registry.py's _TF_SECONDS had no "5m" entry, even though Dexter
scans crypto on 5m (dexter.py's own SCAN_TFS_CRYPTO includes it, and dexter's
own TF_SECONDS table already has it). Every 5m ray's _bars_since silently
fell back to 1h's 3600 sec/bar -- 12x too coarse -- corrupting every
projection, touch/break/pierce evaluation, horizon timestamp, and stale-
retirement check computed for that timeframe. Separately, scan_pair_tf's
incremental ray-touch bar walk used a bare `primary_df.tail(10)`, silently
dropping history whenever more than 10 bars elapsed between scans for a ray
(a restart, a skipped cycle, etc.).

WHAT CHANGED AND WHY:

1. ray_registry.py -- _TF_SECONDS extended to {"1m":60, "5m":300, "15m":900,
   "30m":1800, "1h":3600, "4h":14400, "1d":86400} ("5m" was the actual gap;
   "1m" added defensively, per the task, though nothing scans it today). New
   comment cites the real reference tables after reading dexter.py rather
   than trusting the phase text's own naming: dexter's actual per-pair scan
   cadence lives in SCAN_TFS_CRYPTO/SCAN_TFS_FOREX (dexter.py ~4125-4126),
   NOT TIMEFRAMES_FOREX_STOCK (~4106) as the phase text named -- that table
   turned out to be a different, narrower list (["1h","4h"]) that only
   drives the horizontal S/R validated-level submodel's multi-TF loop, not
   which timeframes actually reach scan_pair_tf/reconcile(). This is exactly
   the "two things with similar names, only one is what you think" trap the
   preamble warns about -- caught by reading both call sites (dexter.py
   ~9354 vs ~13731) before writing the comment, not by trusting either name.
   Values cross-checked against dexter's own TF_SECONDS (dexter.py ~4113),
   the correct reference for the seconds-per-bar numbers themselves.

   _bars_since now prints one `[ray_registry] WARNING: unknown timeframe...`
   line the first time it ever sees a timeframe string absent from
   _TF_SECONDS, via a new module-level `_unknown_tf_warned` seen-set (not a
   per-call check) -- loud once per unknown value per process, then silent,
   still falling back to 1h so nothing crashes.

2. ray_registry.py -- new constant R7_5M_FIX_DEPLOY_TS = 1783987200
   (2026-07-14 00:00:00 UTC, this phase's ship date, hardcoded rather than
   computed from "now" so re-running the self-test or restarting dexter.py
   days later doesn't move the cutoff) and new function _retire_pre_r7_5m():
   retires (state -> "RETIRED", one ray_identity_log.jsonl line citing
   "pre-R7 5m bar-math fix") any RayRecord with timeframe=="5m" and
   born_ts < R7_5M_FIX_DEPLOY_TS, guarded by `state != "RETIRED"` so it only
   ever fires once per record. Records of every other timeframe are
   completely untouched (the condition checks timeframe=="5m" explicitly).

   Deliberately wired into reconcile() (called once per _retire_stale(), now
   sweeping the WHOLE registry dict rather than just the caller's own
   (symbol, timeframe, side) key) rather than into load_registry() itself --
   see the SECOND-PASS REVIEW below for why load_registry() would have been
   an actual hard-rule violation, not just a stylistic choice.

   ray_registry.json does not currently exist on disk (checked directly --
   the file is absent, meaning the bot has genuinely never been run, exactly
   as every phase's hard rule requires) -- so there are, as of this commit,
   ZERO 5m records of any kind to retire. The guard is implemented and
   self-tested anyway per the task's own instruction, since the file may
   gain 5m records between this commit and Kev's restart if his own running
   instance (outside this session) mints any under the old code first. One
   edge case worth naming honestly: R7_5M_FIX_DEPLOY_TS is pinned to today's
   date, so a 5m ray minted by an OLD, still-running process AFTER midnight
   UTC today but BEFORE Kev actually restarts with this fix would carry a
   born_ts on the correct side of the cutoff (i.e., NOT retired) despite
   still using the buggy math. Given the registry file's total absence
   confirms no instance has been minting rays during this entire build, this
   isn't a live risk today, but it's a real, narrow gap in the guard's logic
   that would only bite if Kev's setup deviates from "never run until
   restart."

3. dexter.py -- one new constant, RAY_GAP_LOOKBACK_BARS = 50, defined
   alongside RAY_ALERT_DEDUP_WINDOW_SEC (dexter.py ~11169, the only other
   ray-specific constant already living in dexter.py itself, since every
   other ray tolerance/threshold belongs in ray_registry.py). The literal
   `primary_df.tail(10)` inside scan_pair_tf's ray wiring (confirmed exactly
   one match in the whole file before editing) now reads
   `primary_df.tail(RAY_GAP_LOOKBACK_BARS)`. Both old and new values only
   ever affect bars STRICTLY newer than the ray's last-seen timestamp (the
   `if _bts <= _prior_ts: continue` filter inside the loop is unchanged) --
   the only behavior difference is when MORE than 10 (but <=50) bars have
   elapsed since a ray's last scan, which now get walked instead of silently
   dropped. This is the intended fix, not a new risk: nothing about the
   touch/break-state math itself changed, only how much incremental history
   is fed into it.

4. ray_registry.py -- 5 new self-test checks (41 -> 46):
     14a: _bars_since(T0, T0+3600, "5m") == 12.0, and _project_value moves a
          5m ray by slope_raw * 12 over that same hour -- proves the actual
          bar-math fix, not just that the table has a new key.
     14b: constructs a registry with a pre-R7 5m record and a 15m record of
          identical born_ts, calls reconcile() for a THIRD, unrelated key,
          and confirms the 5m record is RETIRED while the 15m one is
          untouched -- proves the whole-registry sweep (not just the
          currently-reconciled key) and the timeframe=="5m" filter both work.
     14c: calls _bars_since twice with an unrecognized timeframe ("3m") and
          confirms the warning string appears in captured stdout exactly
          once, not twice.

BENEFIT: 5m rays (Dexter's fastest-scanned crypto timeframe) now get the
same trustworthy touch/break/pierce/horizon math every other timeframe
already had -- previously every single one was silently 12x wrong with zero
signal anything was off. A restart or a skipped scan cycle no longer quietly
loses up to 40 bars of legitimate touch history. Any FUTURE missing-
timeframe bug of this exact shape will now print a warning instead of
silently corrupting math again.

SECOND-PASS REVIEW (Lead AI Quant Strategist / Senior Python Architect pass,
re-reading the diff cold): traced everything touched directly (_TF_SECONDS,
_bars_since, R7_5M_FIX_DEPLOY_TS, _retire_pre_r7_5m, reconcile(),
RAY_GAP_LOOKBACK_BARS, the tail() call site) and indirectly:
  - The one finding that actually changed the design mid-implementation:
    the task's Task 2 wording ("on load, any record... gets state=
    'RETIRED' and one identity-log line") reads most naturally as logic
    belonging inside load_registry() itself. I started to implement it
    there, then stopped and reconsidered against this build's own hard
    rule -- "New Flask routes are READ-ONLY... must never mutate registry
    state, tallies, or identity logs... a chart refresh must leave zero
    trace in trust data." load_registry() is called by BOTH the read-only
    /api/rays route AND the write-capable scan wiring; it has no way to
    know which kind of caller invoked it. If the retirement's identity-log
    write lived inside load_registry(), the very FIRST /api/rays chart
    refresh after a restart (before any scan has run) would write a new
    ray_identity_log.jsonl line purely from a GET request -- an unambiguous
    violation, since "identity logs" is one of the three things named
    explicitly in that rule. Re-designed instead around reconcile() (the
    one function that already both logs AND is only ever called from the
    write-capable scan path, under REGISTRY_LOCK, immediately followed by
    save_registry()) -- extended it to sweep the FULL registry dict
    (already an existing parameter, not just its own key) rather than
    adding a second code path. Verified via grep that reconcile() has
    exactly one call site in dexter.py (the scan wiring) and that every
    OTHER load_registry() caller (api_rays, ask_chev_to_judge, _maybe_send_
    ray_break_alert, ask_chev_manage_trade) never calls reconcile() --
    confirming none of them can trigger the log write.
  - Verified ordering inside reconcile(): _retire_pre_r7_5m() runs BEFORE
    _reconcile_decision() (the match-or-mint step). This is load-bearing,
    not incidental -- if a pre-R7 5m ray's own symbol/tf/side gets scanned
    again, retiring it FIRST means _reconcile_decision's own `if ray.state
    != "LIVE": continue` filter correctly excludes it from matching, so a
    brand-new ray mints fresh under the same key on the very same call --
    satisfying "fresh 5m rays mint cleanly afterward" immediately, not one
    scan cycle late.
  - Confirmed the guard is genuinely idempotent with no separate seen-set
    needed (unlike the unknown-timeframe warning, which has no natural
    persisted marker): REGISTRY_LOCK already serializes every scan's full
    load->reconcile->save sequence process-wide (per the module's own
    docstring), so the first successful cycle that retires+saves a record
    is guaranteed to complete before any other thread's reconcile() call
    can observe the same on-disk "not yet RETIRED" state -- no duplicate
    log lines are possible.
  - Confirmed no existing self-test used timeframe "5m" anywhere before this
    phase (grepped the whole file) -- the new retirement logic can't have
    silently altered any pre-existing test's fixtures. Confirmed T0
    (1_700_000_000, used throughout the pre-existing suite) predates
    R7_5M_FIX_DEPLOY_TS, which would matter if any old fixture used "5m" --
    it doesn't, so this is inert.
  - Verified `ray.state == "RETIRED"` is handled identically everywhere
    downstream regardless of WHY a ray was retired: select_live() and every
    state-machine function already gate on `state != "LIVE": continue"` or
    `state == "LIVE"` checks that pre-date this phase (used identically by
    the existing RAY_STALE_BARS path) -- an R7-retired ray is invisible to
    narration/selection/matching through the exact same, already-proven
    mechanism, not a new code path that needed its own new gating.
  - Noted (not fixed, by design): reconcile()'s single `line["ts"] =
    current_bar_ts` stamp applies uniformly to every log line generated
    during a call, including a different symbol/timeframe's R7 retirement
    entry -- so an R7 RETIRED line can carry a `ts` from whichever unrelated
    scan happened to trigger the sweep. This exactly matches _retire_stale's
    own pre-existing behavior (same stamp, same imprecision) -- not a new
    inconsistency introduced by this phase.
No issues required a fix beyond the load_registry()-vs-reconcile() redesign
above, which was caught and corrected before ever being tested, not shipped
and later patched.
